Waqf — Endowment

8 min
Trustee Cannot Divert Waqf Oil Revenue
Ruling on trustee's duty in a specific waqf for oil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a trustee of a waqf for mosque oil cannot spend the revenue on other purposes, and identify the condition that makes the waqf valid.

Core Idea
A waqf trustee is bound by the founder's specification; diverting funds is haram.

This lesson is based on a passage from al-Khaniyya, a key Hanafi legal work. It addresses a waqf created for the purpose of providing oil for mosque lamps. The text clarifies the trustee's obligation to use the income exclusively for that purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqf subject
The waqf is a room dedicated for the oil of the mosque lamp. This is a specific type of waqf where the purpose is clearly defined.
2
Confirm the validity condition
The waqf becomes valid when the property is handed over to the trustee (al-mutawalli). Delivery is a key condition.
The text says 'إذا سلمها إلى المتولي' (if he hands it over to the trustee).
3
State the trustee's restriction
The trustee cannot spend the revenue (al-ghalla) on anything other than oil. This is a strict limitation.
The prohibition is explicit: 'وليس للمتولي أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن'.
4
Apply the analogy
Similarly, if something is endowed for an imam of a mosque, it cannot be spent on others. The same principle applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : لو جعل حجرته لدهن سراج المسجد ولم يزد صارت وقفاً على المسجد إذا سلمها إلى المتولي وعليه الفتوى، وليس للمتولي أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن اهـ . فعلى هذا الموقوف على إمام للمسجد لا يصرف لغيره. وفي الخانية : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لأعمال البر هل يجوز أن يسرج المسجد منه؟ قال الفقيه أبو بكر: يجوز ولا يجوز أن يزاد على سراج المسجد لأن ذلك إسراف، سواء كان ذلك في رمضان أو غيره، ولا يزين المسجد بهذه الوصية .اهـ. ومقتضاه منع الكثرة الواقعة في رمضان في مساجد القاهرة ولو شرط الواقف لأن شرطه لا يعتبر في المعصية. وفي القنية : وإسراج السرج الكثيرة في السكك والأسواق ليلة البراءة بدعة، وكذا في المساجد ويضمن القيم، وكذا الجامع الذي شرط فيه تدريس إذا غاب مدرسه لم يقطع من حيث كونه جامعاً ويتعطل من حيث كونه مدرسة فيجب تقديمه من هذه الحيثية. قوله : (والشاد) قيل هو الدعجي، قلت: ويشهد له ما في القاموس : الإشادة رفع الصوت بالشيء وتعريف الضالة والإهلال والشياد الدعاء بالإبل وذلك الطيب بالجلد. قوله : ( ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي قال في الدر المنتقى : المزملاتي هو الشاوي بعرف أهل الشام . وذكر الشرنبلالي في شرح الوهبانية أن ظهور شمول تقديم البواب والمزملاتي وخادم المطهرة مما لا يتردد فيه اهـ. قوله : (وليس للمتولى أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن) سيأتي لهذا زيادة في
In al-Khaniyya: If someone makes his room for the oil of the mosque lamp and does not increase, it becomes an endowment for the mosque if he hands it over to the trustee, and the fatwa is upon this. The trustee cannot spend the revenue on anything other than oil. End quote. Based on this, what is endowed for an imam of the mosque cannot be spent on other than him. In al-Khaniyya: A man bequeathed a third of his wealth for charitable deeds. Is it permissible to provide lamps for the mosque from it? The faqih Abu Bakr said: It is permissible, but it is not permissible to exceed the usual mosque lighting because that is wastefulness, whether in Ramadan or otherwise. The mosque should not be decorated with this bequest. End quote. Its implication prevents the excessive (lamps) occurring in Ramadan in the mosques of Cairo, even if the waqf founder stipulated it, because his stipulation is not considered in sin. In al-Qunyah: Lighting many lamps in alleys and markets on the Night of Bara'ah is an innovation. Likewise in mosques, and the custodian is liable. Also the Friday mosque in which teaching was stipulated, if its teacher is absent, it does not cease to be a Friday mosque, but from the perspective of being a school it becomes idle, so he should be given precedence from this perspective. His statement: (And the shadd – it is said it is the announcer (da'aji). I say: What supports this is in al-Qamus: al-ishada is raising the voice with something and announcing a lost item and raising the voice in talbiya; and al-shiyad is calling camels; and the pleasant smell on leather. His statement: 'And doubt arises regarding the doorman and the muzammilati.' In al-Durr al-Muntaqa: Al-muzammilati is the seller of grilled meat in the terminology of the people of Sham. Al-Shurunbalali mentioned in Sharh al-Wahbaniyya that the clarity of the inclusion of the doorman, the muzammilati, and the servant of the water place is not to be hesitated about. End quote. His statement: 'And the trustee cannot spend the revenue on other than oil' – more on this will follow.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage contains a series of rulings related to the specific use of waqf funds for oil (lighting) and the prohibition of excess. The first ruling from al-Khaniyya establishes that if someone dedicates a room for the purpose of providing oil for the mosque lamp, this becomes a valid waqf upon delivery to the trustee. The trustee is then bound to spend the income from that property only on oil for the mosque; he cannot divert it to other uses. This is analogized to a waqf specifically for an imam: it cannot be spent on anyone else. The second ruling deals with a bequest for charitable deeds (a'maal al-birr). The faqih Abu Bakr rules that it is permissible to use such a bequest for mosque lighting, but only up to the usual amount; exceeding that is considered wastefulness (israf), even in Ramadan. Furthermore, the mosque should not be decorated with such a bequest. This implies that the excessive lighting seen in Cairo mosques during Ramadan is prohibited, even if the waqf founder stipulated it, because conditions stipulating sin are invalid. The third ruling from al-Qunyah declares that lighting many lamps in streets, markets, and mosques on the Night of Bara'ah is an innovation (bid'ah), and the custodian is liable for any waste. The text then digresses to define 'shadd' and address the doubt about the doorman and water carrier, concluding with the note that more will follow on the trustee's restriction.

Key Terms
متولي (mutawallī): Trustee or administrator of a waqf; responsible for managing the waqf property and disbursing its revenue according to the founder's conditions.
غلة (ghalla): Revenue or income generated from waqf property (e.g., rent, produce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ruling from al-Khaniyya, what condition must be met for the room to become a valid waqf for mosque oil?
A) The room must be large enough to hold oil.
B) The room must be handed over to the trustee.
C) The trustee must agree to the waqf.
D) The mosque must be built first.

Key Takeaway
A waqf trustee must adhere strictly to the founder's specified purpose; diverting funds is prohibited and considered a violation of trust.

Prohibition of Excessive Spending on Mosque Lighting
Fatwa on excessive mosque lighting and invalidity of sinful conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why exceeding the usual mosque lighting is haram according to the Hanafi school, even if the waqf founder stipulates it.

Core Idea
Excess lighting is israf and any condition promoting sin is invalid in waqf.

This lesson covers the second ruling from the same passage, addressing a bequest for charitable deeds used for mosque lighting. The fatwa of Abu Bakr al-Faqih establishes that while it is permissible to use such funds for lighting, it is not permissible to exceed the usual amount because that constitutes wastefulness (israf). Furthermore, even if the waqf founder stipulates excess lighting, the stipulation is invalid because it involves sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
Can a bequest for charitable deeds (a'maal al-birr) be used for mosque lighting? This is the scenario in the text.
2
Determine the permissibility
The faqih Abu Bakr rules: Yes, it is permissible (yajooz) to use the bequest for mosque lighting.
This is the default permission.
3
Apply the limitation
It is not permissible to exceed the usual amount of lighting because that is israf (wastefulness). This applies in Ramadan and other times.
The proof is the explicit statement: 'لا يجوز أن يزاد على سراج المسجد لأن ذلك إسراف'.
4
Consider the stipulation
Even if the waqf founder stipulates extra lighting, the condition is not considered because it involves a sin (ma'siya). The founder's condition is invalid when it entails something haram.
The text says: 'ولو شرط الواقف لأن شرطه لا يعتبر في المعصية'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : لو جعل حجرته لدهن سراج المسجد ولم يزد صارت وقفاً على المسجد إذا سلمها إلى المتولي وعليه الفتوى، وليس للمتولي أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن اهـ . فعلى هذا الموقوف على إمام للمسجد لا يصرف لغيره. وفي الخانية : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لأعمال البر هل يجوز أن يسرج المسجد منه؟ قال الفقيه أبو بكر: يجوز ولا يجوز أن يزاد على سراج المسجد لأن ذلك إسراف، سواء كان ذلك في رمضان أو غيره، ولا يزين المسجد بهذه الوصية .اهـ. ومقتضاه منع الكثرة الواقعة في رمضان في مساجد القاهرة ولو شرط الواقف لأن شرطه لا يعتبر في المعصية. وفي القنية : وإسراج السرج الكثيرة في السكك والأسواق ليلة البراءة بدعة، وكذا في المساجد ويضمن القيم، وكذا الجامع الذي شرط فيه تدريس إذا غاب مدرسه لم يقطع من حيث كونه جامعاً ويتعطل من حيث كونه مدرسة فيجب تقديمه من هذه الحيثية. قوله : (والشاد) قيل هو الدعجي، قلت: ويشهد له ما في القاموس : الإشادة رفع الصوت بالشيء وتعريف الضالة والإهلال والشياد الدعاء بالإبل وذلك الطيب بالجلد. قوله : ( ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي قال في الدر المنتقى : المزملاتي هو الشاوي بعرف أهل الشام . وذكر الشرنبلالي في شرح الوهبانية أن ظهور شمول تقديم البواب والمزملاتي وخادم المطهرة مما لا يتردد فيه اهـ. قوله : (وليس للمتولى أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن) سيأتي لهذا زيادة في

Commentary
This passage contains a series of rulings related to the specific use of waqf funds for oil (lighting) and the prohibition of excess. The first ruling from al-Khaniyya establishes that if someone dedicates a room for the purpose of providing oil for the mosque lamp, this becomes a valid waqf upon delivery to the trustee. The trustee is then bound to spend the income from that property only on oil for the mosque; he cannot divert it to other uses. This is analogized to a waqf specifically for an imam: it cannot be spent on anyone else. The second ruling deals with a bequest for charitable deeds (a'maal al-birr). The faqih Abu Bakr rules that it is permissible to use such a bequest for mosque lighting, but only up to the usual amount; exceeding that is considered wastefulness (israf), even in Ramadan. The text then digresses to define 'shadd' and address the doubt about the doorman and water carrier, concluding with the note that more will follow on the trustee's restriction.

Key Terms
إسراف (isrāf): Excessive spending beyond what is needed; here it refers to increasing mosque lighting beyond the usual amount, which is legally prohibited.
بدعة (bid'ah): Religious innovation; here specifically the practice of lighting many lamps on Lailat al-Bara'ah, which is condemned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf founder stipulates lighting extra lamps during Ramadan, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) It must be followed because the founder's conditions are binding.
B) It is permissible but not recommended.
C) It is prohibited because it involves israf, and the condition is invalid.
D) It is allowed only if the mosque has surplus funds.

Key Takeaway
Excessive spending in mosque lighting is israf and therefore haram; waqf conditions that entail sin are null and void.

Proportional Entitlement of Mosque Workers from Waqf
Listing the ruling on pay and a Shafi'i ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on compensating mosque workers from waqf income and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Mosque workers are paid proportionally to work done, not a fixed amount, unless the endower specifies otherwise.

When a waqf is established for a mosque, after maintenance the income is spent on various functionaries. This passage clarifies that their entitlement is based on actual work, not a predetermined stipend, especially if the endower's condition is vague. This principle is juxtaposed with a Shafi'i view that denies any payment if the work condition is unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on compensation
The text states that a worker (e.g., teacher or student) deserves compensation in proportion to the work he performs, not the full amount if the work is less.
This is a general Hanafi principle for waqf beneficiaries.
2
Understand the basis of the ruling
The nazir must consider both the endower's stipulation and the actual work done. The income is divided accordingly.
The endower's condition is binding, but if ambiguous, work determines share.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The text notes that some Shafi'is (e.g., Ibn al-Subki) hold that if the work condition is unknown, the worker deserves nothing.
The Hanafi view is more flexible, granting proportional pay.
4
Apply to modern scenarios
This ruling applies to any paid religious functionary in a mosque, such as a part-time imam or a cleaner.
The key is to assess actual hours or duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكم المتعلم والمدرس في المسألتين سواء اهـ. واستفيد من قوله لا يستحق غلتهما بتمامها أنه يستحق بقدر عمله وهي كثيرة الوقوع في أصحاب الوظائف في زماننا وحاصله أنه ينظر إلى ما شرطه الواقف له وعليه من العمل ويقسم المشروط على عمله خلافاً لبعض الشافعية فإنه يقول : إذا لم يعلم المشروط لا يستحق شيئاً من المشروط كما ذكره ابن السبكي. وقوله «ثم السراج» بكسر السين أي القناديل ومراده مع زيتها . . جرت والبساط - بكسر الباء - أي الحصير ويلحق بهما معلوم خادمها وهو الوقاد والفراش فيقدمان. وتعبيره بـ ثم دون الواو يدل على أنهما مؤخران عن الإمام والمدرس. وفي القنية : لو اشترى بساطاً نفيساً من غلته جاز إذا استغنى المسجد عن العمارة اهـ. وقوله «إلى آخر المصالح» أي مصالح المسجد فيدخل المؤذن والناظر لأنا قدمنا أنهم من المصالح، وقدمنا أن الخطيب داخل تحت الإمام لأنه إمام الجامع فتحصل أن الشعائر التي تقدم في الصرف مطلقاً بعد العمارة الإمام والخطيب والمدرس والوقاد والفراش والمؤذن والناظر وثمن القناديل والزيت والحصر، ويلحق بثمن الزيت والحصر ثمن ماء الوضوء أو أجرة حمله أو كلفة نقله من البئر إلى الميضأة فليس المباشر والشاهد والجابي والشاد وخازن الكتب من الشعائر، وقد العادة بمصر في ديوان المحاسبة بتقديمهم مع المذكورين أولاً وليس شرعياً، ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي .
And the ruling of the student and the teacher in both issues is the same. And it is understood from his statement 'he does not deserve its entire yield' that he deserves in proportion to his work, and this is frequent among functionaries today. The gist is that one considers what the endower stipulated for him and what work is required of him, and the stipulated amount is divided according to his work, contrary to some Shafi'is who say: if the stipulated work is not known, he deserves nothing from the stipulated amount, as mentioned by Ibn al-Subki. Then his statement 'then the lamp' with kasra on the sin means the lanterns, and he intends along with their oil. 'And the mat' with kasra on the ba means the rush mat, and joined to them are the known servant of the mosque, namely the stoker (al-waqqad) and the spreader (al-farrash), so they are given priority. And his expression 'then' instead of 'and' indicates that they are deferred after the imam and the teacher. In al-Qunyah: if one buys a valuable mat from its yield, it is permissible if the mosque is self-sufficient regarding maintenance. And his statement 'up to the other interests' means the interests of the mosque, so the muezzin and the overseer enter, for we have stated that they are among the interests. And we have stated that the khatib is included under the imam because he is the imam of the Friday mosque. Thus it results that the rituals (sha'air) that are given priority in spending absolutely after maintenance are: the imam, the khatib, the teacher, the stoker, the spreader, the muezzin, and the overseer, and the price of lanterns, oil, and mats. And attached to the price of oil and mats is the price of water for ablution, or the hire of carrying it, or the cost of transferring it from the well to the place of ablution. So the direct executor (mubashir), the witness (shahid), the collector (jabi), the shadd, and the librarian (khazin al-kutub) are not among the rituals. And the custom in Egypt in the accounting office is to give them priority along with those mentioned first, and this is not legal. And confusion occurs regarding the gatekeeper (bawwab) and the water-carrier (muzammilati).
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the priorities of spending mosque waqf income after maintenance. It begins by clarifying that for those who work in the mosque (teacher, student), their entitlement is proportional to their actual work, not a fixed amount, contrary to some Shafi'is (like Ibn al-Subki) who say if the work condition is unknown, they get nothing. Then it explains the order: first the imam (and khatib included under him), then the teacher (mudarris), then the lamp (siraj, meaning lanterns with oil), then the mat (bisat, meaning rush mats). The stoker (waqqad) and spreader (farrash) are joined to the lamp and mat respectively, but they are deferred after the imam and teacher, as indicated by the word 'then'. Then other mosque interests (masalih) like muezzin and overseer (nazir) follow. The passage explicitly excludes from the 'rituals' (sha'air) the direct executor, witness, collector, shadd, and librarian, though custom in Egypt wrongly prioritizes them. It also notes uncertainty about gatekeeper and water-carrier. This is a ruling statement with explanatory commentary.

Key Terms
الشعائر (ash-sha'air): The recognized recipients of mosque waqf income who have priority after maintenance.
السراج (as-siraj): The lamp/lantern of the mosque, often including its oil.
البساط (al-bisat): The mat or carpet used in the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a mosque waqf stipulates a salary for the imam but does not specify the work amount, how is the imam compensated?
A) The full salary because the condition is general.
B) Proportional to the work he actually performs.
C) Nothing, because the condition is void.
D) It is left to the imam's discretion.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh mandates proportional pay for mosque workers from waqf, ensuring justice even when conditions are vague.

Priority Order of Spending Mosque Waqf Proceeds After Maintenance
Ordering the recipients of mosque waqf income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the correct sequence of priorities for spending mosque waqf income after maintenance, and identify which roles are included or excluded.

Core Idea
After maintenance, the order is: imam (including khatib), teacher, lamp, mat, then other interests (muezzin, nazir).

This passage provides the authoritative Hanafi order of spending from a mosque's waqf revenue. The sequence is not arbitrary but derived from the endower's conditions and the necessities of the mosque. Understanding this order is crucial for the nazir (overseer) to comply with Shariah and avoid illegal customs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline: after maintenance
All spending on sha'air (ritual functions) occurs only after the mosque's physical maintenance (carpenter, repairs) is covered.
Maintenance of the building takes precedence over all other expenses.
2
List the first two: imam and teacher
The imam (and khatib included) comes first, then the teacher (mudarris).
The khatib is considered under the imam because he leads the Friday sermon.
3
Note the next two: lamp and mat
After the imam and teacher, the lamp (siraj, including oil) and mat (bisat, including substitutes like rush mats) are next. Their servants (stoker, spreader) are included but deferred after the lamp and mat.
The use of 'then' (ثم) shows these are after the first two.
4
Identify other interests (masalih)
Then come other mosque interests like the muezzin and nazir.
Muezzin is explicitly mentioned; nazir is also included as a necessity.
5
Recognize exclusions
Roles like the direct executor (mubashir), witness (shahid), collector (jabi), shadd, and librarian are not among the sha'air. Custom in Egypt giving them priority is illegal.
Gatekeeper and water-carrier are ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكم المتعلم والمدرس في المسألتين سواء اهـ. واستفيد من قوله لا يستحق غلتهما بتمامها أنه يستحق بقدر عمله وهي كثيرة الوقوع في أصحاب الوظائف في زماننا وحاصله أنه ينظر إلى ما شرطه الواقف له وعليه من العمل ويقسم المشروط على عمله خلافاً لبعض الشافعية فإنه يقول : إذا لم يعلم المشروط لا يستحق شيئاً من المشروط كما ذكره ابن السبكي. وقوله «ثم السراج» بكسر السين أي القناديل ومراده مع زيتها . . جرت والبساط - بكسر الباء - أي الحصير ويلحق بهما معلوم خادمها وهو الوقاد والفراش فيقدمان. وتعبيره بـ ثم دون الواو يدل على أنهما مؤخران عن الإمام والمدرس. وفي القنية : لو اشترى بساطاً نفيساً من غلته جاز إذا استغنى المسجد عن العمارة اهـ. وقوله «إلى آخر المصالح» أي مصالح المسجد فيدخل المؤذن والناظر لأنا قدمنا أنهم من المصالح، وقدمنا أن الخطيب داخل تحت الإمام لأنه إمام الجامع فتحصل أن الشعائر التي تقدم في الصرف مطلقاً بعد العمارة الإمام والخطيب والمدرس والوقاد والفراش والمؤذن والناظر وثمن القناديل والزيت والحصر، ويلحق بثمن الزيت والحصر ثمن ماء الوضوء أو أجرة حمله أو كلفة نقله من البئر إلى الميضأة فليس المباشر والشاهد والجابي والشاد وخازن الكتب من الشعائر، وقد العادة بمصر في ديوان المحاسبة بتقديمهم مع المذكورين أولاً وليس شرعياً، ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي .
And the ruling of the student and the teacher in both issues is the same. And it is understood from his statement 'he does not deserve its entire yield' that he deserves in proportion to his work, and this is frequent among functionaries today. The gist is that one considers what the endower stipulated for him and what work is required of him, and the stipulated amount is divided according to his work, contrary to some Shafi'is who say: if the stipulated work is not known, he deserves nothing from the stipulated amount, as mentioned by Ibn al-Subki. Then his statement 'then the lamp' with kasra on the sin means the lanterns, and he intends along with their oil. 'And the mat' with kasra on the ba means the rush mat, and joined to them are the known servant of the mosque, namely the stoker (al-waqqad) and the spreader (al-farrash), so they are given priority. And his expression 'then' instead of 'and' indicates that they are deferred after the imam and the teacher. In al-Qunyah: if one buys a valuable mat from its yield, it is permissible if the mosque is self-sufficient regarding maintenance. And his statement 'up to the other interests' means the interests of the mosque, so the muezzin and the overseer enter, for we have stated that they are among the interests. And we have stated that the khatib is included under the imam because he is the imam of the Friday mosque. Thus it results that the rituals (sha'air) that are given priority in spending absolutely after maintenance are: the imam, the khatib, the teacher, the stoker, the spreader, the muezzin, and the overseer, and the price of lanterns, oil, and mats. And attached to the price of oil and mats is the price of water for ablution, or the hire of carrying it, or the cost of transferring it from the well to the place of ablution. So the direct executor (mubashir), the witness (shahid), the collector (jabi), the shadd, and the librarian (khazin al-kutub) are not among the rituals. And the custom in Egypt in the accounting office is to give them priority along with those mentioned first, and this is not legal. And confusion occurs regarding the gatekeeper (bawwab) and the water-carrier (muzammilati).
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the priorities of spending mosque waqf income after maintenance. It begins by clarifying that for those who work in the mosque (teacher, student), their entitlement is proportional to their actual work, not a fixed amount, contrary to some Shafi'is (like Ibn al-Subki) who say if the work condition is unknown, they get nothing. Then it explains the order: first the imam (and khatib included under him), then the teacher (mudarris), then the lamp (siraj, meaning lanterns with oil), then the mat (bisat, meaning rush mats). The stoker (waqqad) and spreader (farrash) are joined to the lamp and mat respectively, but they are deferred after the imam and teacher, as indicated by the word 'then'. Then other mosque interests (masalih) like muezzin and overseer (nazir) follow. The passage explicitly excludes from the 'rituals' (sha'air) the direct executor, witness, collector, shadd, and librarian, though custom in Egypt wrongly prioritizes them. It also notes uncertainty about gatekeeper and water-carrier. This is a ruling statement with explanatory commentary.

Key Terms
الشعائر (ash-sha'air): The recognized recipients of mosque waqf income who have priority after maintenance.
السراج (as-siraj): The lamp/lantern of the mosque, often including its oil.
البساط (al-bisat): The mat or carpet used in the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The teacher.
B) The mat.
C) Both equally.
D) Depends on the imam's decision.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of spending mosque waqf proceeds after maintenance is a strict sequence that protects the sacred functions of the mosque and must not be altered by custom.

Buying a Valuable Mat from Mosque Waqf Income
Ruling on conditional permissibility of purchasing valuable mat from mosque waqf income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which it is permissible to purchase a valuable mat from mosque waqf income and explain the underlying legal principle.

Core Idea
Surplus waqf income can beautify a mosque if core maintenance needs are already satisfied.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Qunyah regarding the use of waqf income for purchasing an expensive mat for the mosque. While waqf income is primarily for maintenance, surplus funds can be directed toward improvements that benefit the mosque, provided the basic upkeep is already covered.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its ruling
Identify the act: purchasing a valuable mat from mosque waqf income (ghalla). The ruling is jā'iz (permissible) under a specific condition.
2
Identify the condition
The mosque must be self-sufficient in maintenance, i.e., no pressing need for repair funds. This ensures the primary purpose of the waqf is not neglected.
3
Determine the legal basis
The permissibility derives from the broader principle that surplus waqf income can be used for the mosque's benefit, including beautification, when basic needs are met.
This reflects a maslahah (public interest) approach within Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize the source authority
The ruling comes from al-Qunyah, a later Hanafi fatwa collection (fatawa mutakhkhirin), indicating it is the operative position (mufta bihi).
Al-Qunyah is a well-known source for Hanafi fatwa rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : لو اشترى بساطاً نفيساً من غلته جاز إذا استغنى المسجد عن العمارة اهـ.
And in al-Qunyah: if one buys a valuable mat from its yield, it is permissible if the mosque is self-sufficient regarding maintenance.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This is a discrete ruling from al-Qunyah cited in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It states that the nazir (overseer) may purchase a valuable mat from the waqf income (ghalla) if the mosque does not need that money for repair (i.e. it is already well-maintained). The ruling is permissive because the mat is for the benefit of the mosque, and since there is no pressing need for repair, the surplus can be used for improvements or beautification.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The income or produce of the waqf property.
البساط النفيس (al-bisat an-nafis): An expensive mat or carpet for the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever the nazir wishes
B) Only if the endower explicitly allowed it
C) If the mosque is self-sufficient regarding maintenance
D) During Ramadan only

Key Takeaway
If a mosque's maintenance needs are already met, surplus waqf income may be used to purchase valuable items that enhance the mosque, such as an expensive mat.

Excessive Lighting in Mosques: Bid'ah and Liability of the Nazir
Fatwa from al-Qunyah on excessive lighting and waqf liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on excessive lighting in mosques during Ramadan and identify when the nazir becomes liable for waste of waqf property.

Core Idea
Wasting waqf property even for religious celebration is prohibited; the nazir must compensate from his own wealth.

Al-Qunyah's ruling addresses a practice common in his time: lighting many lamps in streets and mosques on Laylat al-Bara'ah and during Ramadan. This is not merely a matter of etiquette but involves the legal liability of the waqf administrator (nazir). Understanding this ruling helps us grasp the Hanafi position on financial responsibility within awqaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is lighting many lamps in alleys, markets, and mosques on Laylat al-Bara'ah and during Ramadan. The ruling: it is a bid'ah (innovation) and the nazir is liable (yadman) for any waste.
The term bid'ah here is used in a negative sense because it involves waste of waqf funds.
2
Determine the responsible party
The nazir (administrator of the waqf) is responsible for authorized spending. If he exceeds the norm, he must personally compensate the waqf.
The liability is personal, not from the waqf funds.
3
Distinguish permissible vs. impermissible lighting
Lighting at the mosque door in the alley or market is permissible. It is the excessive, wasteful nature that makes it prohibited.
The distinction is based on customary need and avoidance of israf (extravagance).
4
Apply the broader waqf principle
The ruling illustrates a key waqf principle: the nazir may only spend on what is stipulated or customary; any deviation that wastes funds is prohibited and incurs personal liability.
This protects the waqf corpus from mismanagement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : وإسراج السرج الكثيرة في السكك والأسواق ليلة البراءة بدعة، وكذا في المساجد ويضمن القيم، وكذا الجامع الذي شرط فيه تدريس إذا غاب مدرسه لم يقطع من حيث كونه جامعاً ويتعطل من حيث كونه مدرسة فيجب تقديمه من هذه الحيثية. قوله : (والشاد) قيل هو الدعجي، قلت: ويشهد له ما في القاموس : الإشادة رفع الصوت بالشيء وتعريف الضالة والإهلال والشياد الدعاء بالإبل وذلك الطيب بالجلد. قوله : ( ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي قال في الدر المنتقى : المزملاتي هو الشاوي بعرف أهل الشام . وذكر الشرنبلالي في شرح الوهبانية أن ظهور شمول تقديم البواب والمزملاتي وخادم المطهرة مما لا يتردد فيه اهـ. قوله : (وليس للمتولى أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن) سيأتي لهذا زيادة في ينصر يضمن إذا أسرف في السرج في رمضان وليلة القدر، ويجوز الإسراج على باب المسجد في السكة أو السوق ولو اشترى من مال المسجد شمعاً في رمضان يضمن. قلت: وهذا إذا لم الواقف عليه ولو أوصى بثلث ماله أن ينفق على بيت المقدس جاز وينفق في سراجه ونحوه. قال هشام فدل هذا على أنه يجوز أن ينفق من مال المسجد على قناديله وسرجه له والنفط والزيت اهـ
And in al-Qunyah: lighting many lamps in alleys and markets on the night of Bara'ah is an innovation, and likewise in mosques, and the nazir is liable. And likewise a mosque which has a condition of teaching, if its teacher is absent, it is not discontinued from being a mosque, but it is idle from being a school, so it should be given precedence from this aspect. His statement: (and al-Shadd) it is said it is al-Da'aji? I say: and it is witnessed by what is in al-Qamus: al-ishada is raising the voice with something, and announcing a lost object, and al-ihlal, and al-shiyad is calling out to camels, and that perfume with skin. His statement: (and confusion occurs regarding the gatekeeper and the muzammilati) al-Durr al-Muntaqa said: al-muzammilati is the roaster (al-shawi) in the custom of the people of Sham. And Shurunbulali mentioned in Sharh al-Wahbaniyyah that the appearance of including the gatekeeper, the muzammilati, and the servant of the latrine (khadim al-mutahhara) is not doubted. His statement: (and it is not for the nazir to spend the yield on other than oil) there will come for this an addition in... He is liable if he is extravagant in lighting in Ramadan and Laylat al-Qadr, and it is permissible to light at the door of the mosque in the alley or the market. And if one buys candles from the mosque's money in Ramadan, he is liable. I say: and this is if the endower did not [specify?] it. And if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to spend on Bayt al-Maqdis, it is permissible and he spends on its lamps and the like. Hisham said: so this indicates that it is permissible to spend from the mosque's money on its lanterns and lamps, and on naphtha and oil.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage combines several rulings. First, al-Qunyah states that excessive lighting in public streets and mosques on the night of Bara'ah (mid-Sha'ban) is an innovation (bid'ah), and the nazir is liable (yadman) for such waste. Similarly, extravagance in Ramadan and Laylat al-Qadr results in liability. However, lighting at the mosque door in the alley or market is permissible. The text then returns to the discussion of who qualifies as 'rituals' (sha'air), mentioning definitions of 'shadd' and the uncertainty about gatekeeper and water-carrier. Shurunbulali's opinion is that these are included. Then a rule that the nazir cannot divert waqf income to other than oil if the waqf is for oil. The last part deals with a bequest for Bayt al-Maqdis and spending on its lamps. The overall theme is the proper use of mosque waqf funds and avoidance of waste.

Key Terms
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion; here applied to excessive lighting on the night of Bara'ah.
يضمن (yadman): He is liable to compensate from his own property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Qunyah, what is the legal consequence for a nazir who lights many lamps in the mosque during Ramadan beyond the customary amount?
A) The act is recommended because it honors the month.
B) The nazir is not liable if the mosque benefits.
C) The nazir must personally compensate for the waste.
D) Only the candles are forfeited, not the nazir's money.

Key Takeaway
Excessive lighting in mosques using waqf funds is prohibited waste, and the nazir must personally compensate any excess beyond customary needs.

Borrowing with Profit for Urgent Waqf Repair
Seventh issue: borrowing with profit for waqf repair

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a waqf nazir may borrow with riba for urgent repair and explain who bears the increase.

Core Idea
In extreme necessity, a nazir may borrow with profit, but the extra cost is his personal liability.

This lesson examines the seventh issue of the passage, which addresses a difficult scenario: a waqf property (a mosque) is in urgent need of repair, but there is no income and no interest-free loan available. The Hanafi scholars provide a solution that allows borrowing with profit, but with important conditions and consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The waqf (mosque) needs repair but has no yield and cannot borrow without paying interest (riba). This is a case of darurah (necessity).
2
Determine the ruling
The nazir may demolish and rebuild even if neighbors oppose, and he may borrow at a profit (e.g., 10 dirhams for 13). The increase is his own responsibility, not the waqf's.
3
Understand the transaction
The nazir borrows with interest but uses a sale trick (buying a small item) to avoid direct riba. He recovers the principal from the waqf yield later, but the interest is on him.
This is a hila (legal stratagem) to circumvent riba while achieving the waqf's benefit.
4
Note the refutation
Ibn Wahban claimed there was no answer from scholars, but this ruling from al-Qunyah provides a clear answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للمتولى أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهناه السابعة : إذا احتاج الوقف إلى العمارة وليس عنده غلة ولم يتيسر القرض إلا بربح. قال في القنية رامزاً ليوسف الترجماني الصغير : قال البصراء للقيم إن لم تهدم المسجد العام يكون ضرره في القابل أعظم فله هدمه وإن خالفه بعض أهل محلته وليس له التأخير إذا أمكنه العمارة، فلو هدمه ولم يكن فيه غلة للعمارة في الحال فاستقرض العشرة بثلاثة عشر في السنة واشترى من المقرض شيئاً يسيراً بثلاثة دنانير يرجع في غلته بالعشرة وعليه الزيادة اهـ. و به اندفع ما ذكره ابن وهبان من أنه لا جواب للمشايخ فيها. الثامنة في وقف المسجد : أيجوز أن يبنى من غلته منارة؟ قال في الخانية معزياً إلى أبي بكر البلخي : إن كان ذلك من مصلحة المسجد بأن كان أسمع لهم فلا بأس به، وإن كان بحال يسمع الجيران الأذان بغير منارة فلا أرى لهم أن يفعلوا ذلك التاسعة : وقف على عمارة المسجد على أن ما فضل من عمارته فهو للفقراء فاجتمعت الغلة والمسجد غير محتاج إلى العمارة قال الفقيه أبو بكر : تحبس الغلة لأنه ربما يحدث بالمسجد حدث وتصير الأرض بحال لا تغل. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : الجواب كما قال، وعندي لو علم أنه لو اجتمع من الغلة مقدار ما يحتاج الأرض والمسجد إلى العمارة يمكن العمارة بها ويفضل تصرف الزيادة إلى الفقراء على ما شرط الواقف. وفي القنية : ليس للقيم أن يأخذ ما فضل من وجه عمارة المدرسة ديناً ليصرفها إلى الفقراء وإن احتاجوا إليه . وفي الخانية والصحيح ما قال الفقيه أبو الليث أنه ينظر إن اجتمع الغلة مقدار ما لو احتاج الضيعة والمسجد إلى العمارة بعد ذلك يمكن العمارة منها ويبقى شيء تصرف تلك الزيادة إلى الفقراء .اهـ. ريع غلة الوقف للعمارة وثلاثة أرباعها للفقراء لم يجز للقيم أن يصرف ريع العمارة إذا استغنى عنها إلى الفقراء ليسترد ذلك من حصتهم في السنة الثانية اهـ. العاشرة : مسجد تهدم وقد اجتمع من غلته ما يحصل به البناء قال الخصاف : لا ينفق الغلة في البناء لأن الواقف وقف على مرمتها ولم يأمر بأن يبنى هذا المسجد، والفتوى على أنه يجوز البناء بتلك الغلة. ولو كان الوقف على عمارة المسجد هل للقيم أن يشتري سلمًاً المسألة السادسة عشرة. قوله : (قال هشام الخ في الإسعاف ولو أراد المتولي أن يشتري من وقف المسجد دهناً أو حصراً أو أجراً أو حصى ليفرش فيه يجوز إن وسع الواقف في ذلك للقيم بأن قال يفعل ما يراه من مصلحة المسجد، وإن لم يوسع بل وقفه لبناء المسجد وعمارته فليس له أن يشتري ما ذكرنا لأنه ليس من العمارة والبناء. وإن لم يعرف شرطه في ذلك ينظر هذا القيم إلى من
And it is not for the nazir to spend the yield on other than the oil... The seventh issue: if the waqf needs repair and has no yield, and borrowing is not possible except with profit. Al-Qunyah said, alluding to Yusuf al-Turjumani al-Saghir: the intelligent ones said to the nazir: if you do not demolish the mosque this year, its harm next year will be greater, so he may demolish it even if some residents of the neighborhood oppose him, and he cannot delay if he can repair. If he demolishes it and there is no yield for repair immediately, then he borrows ten dirhams at thirteen per year and buys from the lender a small item for three dinars, then he recovers from the yield the ten and the increase is upon him. And by this is refuted what Ibn Wahban mentioned that there is no answer from the scholars on this. The eighth issue: regarding waqf of a mosque: is it permissible to build a minaret from its yield? Al-Khaniyah said, attributing to Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: if that is in the interest of the mosque, such as making the call better heard, there is no harm; if the neighbors can hear the adhan without a minaret, I do not think they should do that. The ninth issue: one makes a waqf for the repair of a mosque, with the condition that whatever remains from its repair goes to the poor. The yield accumulates and the mosque does not need repair. Al-Faqih Abu Bakr said: the yield should be withheld (hubisa) because a need may arise for the mosque and the land may become such that it yields no income. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: the answer is as he said. In my opinion, if one knows that if an amount sufficient for the mosque and land when they later need repair can be accumulated and something remains, then the surplus should be distributed to the poor as the endower stipulated. And in al-Qunyah: it is not for the nazir to take the surplus from the repair of the school as a debt to give to the poor, even if they need it. And in al-Khaniyah, the correct view is what Abu al-Layth said: one looks: if the yield accumulates to an amount such that if the estate and mosque later need repair, repair can be made from it and something remains, then that surplus is given to the poor. ... A yield of waqf: one-fifth for repair, three-fourths for the poor: it is not permissible for the nazir to spend the repair portion when it is not needed to the poor to take it back from their share next year. The tenth issue: a mosque is dilapidated and sufficient yield has accumulated for construction. Al-Khassaf said: the yield should not be spent on construction because the endower made the waqf for repairs, not for building this mosque. But the fatwa is that construction with that yield is permissible. And if the waqf is for repair of the mosque, can the nazir buy a ladder? The sixteenth issue... His statement: (Hisham said... in al-Is'af): If the nazir wants to buy from the mosque waqf oil, mats, bricks, or pebbles to spread, it is permissible if the endower gave broad discretion to the nazir by saying 'do what you see as the interest of the mosque'. If he did not give discretion but rather made the waqf for building and repair only, then he cannot buy what we mentioned because it is not from repair and building. If his condition is not known, one looks...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage contains several distinct rulings on waqf. (1) The nazir may borrow with profit (interest) for urgent repair if no other option, and the increase is his own liability. (2) Building a minaret from mosque waqf is permissible if it serves the interest of making the adhan heard better; otherwise not. (3) If a waqf for mosque repair has surplus that is to go to the poor, the surplus should be saved for future repair needs; only if the accumulated surplus exceeds future needs can it be given to the poor. (4) For a dilapidated mosque, building anew from waqf income is permissible according to fatwa, though al-Khassaf disagreed. (5) The nazir's purchases for the mosque are limited by the endower's stipulation: if broad discretion was given, he may buy items like oil, mats, etc.; if only for building/repair, he cannot; if condition unknown, he must exercise judgment based on interest. The passage ends abruptly at page break. It combines rulings from various sources (al-Qunyah, al-Khaniyah, al-Is'af). Each ruling is a complete legal unit, but here they are presented consecutively.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The overseer or administrator of the waqf, synonymous with nazir.
الربح (al-ribh): Profit or increase, here referring to interest charged on the loan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
In extreme necessity, a nazir may borrow with profit, but the interest is his personal liability, not the waqf's.

Building a Minaret from Mosque Waqf Income
Eighth issue: building minaret from mosque waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition that determines whether a minaret may be built from mosque waqf funds.

Core Idea
A minaret may be built only if it serves the essential interest of the mosque.

The eighth issue discusses whether a minaret can be constructed using the income of a mosque waqf. The answer hinges on whether the minaret serves a genuine need, such as making the adhan audible to the congregation. If the call can already be heard without it, building a minaret is not permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the question
Is it permissible to build a minaret from the waqf income of a mosque?
2
Identify the condition
The permissibility depends on whether the minaret serves the maslahah (interest) of the mosque, such as making the adhan more audible.
3
Apply the condition
If the neighbors can hear the adhan without a minaret, it is not permissible. If it helps, it is permissible.
4
Note the authority
This ruling is from Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, as quoted in al-Khaniyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المسجد العام يكون ضرره في القابل أعظم فله هدمه وإن خالفه بعض أهل محلته وليس له التأخير إذا أمكنه العمارة، فلو هدمه ولم يكن فيه غلة للعمارة في الحال فاستقرض العشرة بثلاثة عشر في السنة واشترى من المقرض إلى أبي بكر البلخي : إن كان ذلك من مصلحة المسجد بأن كان أسمع لهم فلا بأس به، وإن كان بحال يسمع الجيران الأذان بغير منارة فلا أرى لهم أن يفعلوا ذلك التاسعة : وقف على عمارة المسجد على أن ما فضل من عمارته فهو للفقراء فاجتمعت الغلة والمسجد غير محتاج إلى العمارة قال الفقيه أبو بكر : تحبس الغلة لأنه ربما يحدث بالمسجد حدث وتصير الأرض بحال لا تغل. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : الجواب كما قال، وعندي لو علم ليصرفها إلى الفقراء وإن احتاجوا إليه . وفي الخانية والصحيح ما قال الفقيه أبو الليث أنه ينظر إن اجتمع الغلة مقدار ما لو احتاج الضيعة والمسجد إلى العمارة بعد ذلك يمكن العمارة منها ويبقى شيء تصرف تلك الزيادة إلى الفقراء .اهـ. ريع غلة الوقف للعمارة وثلاثة أرباعها للفقراء لم يجز للقيم أن يصرف ريع العمارة إذا استغنى عنها إلى الفقراء ليسترد ذلك من حصتهم في السنة الثانية اهـ. العاشرة : مسجد تهدم وقد اجتمع من غلته ما يحصل به البناء قال الخصاف : لا ينفق الغلة في البناء لأن الواقف وقف على مرمتها ولم يأمر بأن يبنى هذا المسجد، والفتوى على أنه يجوز البناء بتلك الغلة. ولو كان الوقف على عمارة المسجد هل للقيم أن يشتري سلمًاً المسألة السادسة عشرة. قوله : (قال هشام الخ في الإسعاف ولو أراد المتولي أن يشتري من وقف المسجد دهناً أو حصراً أو أجراً أو حصى ليفرش فيه يجوز إن وسع الواقف في ذلك للقيم بأن قال يفعل ما يراه من مصلحة المسجد، وإن لم يوسع بل وقفه لبناء المسجد وعمارته فليس له أن يشتري ما ذكرنا لأنه ليس من العمارة والبناء. وإن لم يعرف شرطه في ذلك ينظر هذا القيم إلى من
And it is not for the nazir to spend the yield on other than the oil... The seventh issue: if the waqf needs repair and has no yield, and borrowing is not possible except with profit. Al-Qunyah said, alluding to Yusuf al-Turjumani al-Saghir: the intelligent ones said to the nazir: if you do not demolish the mosque this year, its harm next year will be greater, so he may demolish it even if some residents of the neighborhood oppose him, and he cannot delay if he can repair. If he demolishes it and there is no yield for repair immediately, then he borrows ten dirhams at thirteen per year and buys from the lender a small item for three dinars, then he recovers from the yield the ten and the increase is upon him. And by this is refuted what Ibn Wahban mentioned that there is no answer from the scholars on this. The eighth issue: regarding waqf of a mosque: is it permissible to build a minaret from its yield? Al-Khaniyah said, attributing to Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: if that is in the interest of the mosque, such as making the call better heard, there is no harm; if the neighbors can hear the adhan without a minaret, I do not think they should do that. The ninth issue: one makes a waqf for the repair of a mosque, with the condition that whatever remains from its repair goes to the poor. The yield accumulates and the mosque does not need repair. Al-Faqih Abu Bakr said: the yield should be withheld (hubisa) because a need may arise for the mosque and the land may become such that it yields no income. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: the answer is as he said. In my opinion, if one knows that if an amount sufficient for the mosque and land when they later need repair can be accumulated and something remains, then the surplus should be distributed to the poor as the endower stipulated. And in al-Qunyah: it is not for the nazir to take the surplus from the repair of the school as a debt to give to the poor, even if they need it. And in al-Khaniyah, the correct view is what Abu al-Layth said: one looks: if the yield accumulates to an amount such that if the estate and mosque later need repair, repair can be made from it and something remains, then that surplus is given to the poor. ... A yield of waqf: one-fifth for repair, three-fourths for the poor: it is not permissible for the nazir to spend the repair portion when it is not needed to the poor to take it back from their share next year. The tenth issue: a mosque is dilapidated and sufficient yield has accumulated for construction. Al-Khassaf said: the yield should not be spent on construction because the endower made the waqf for repairs, not for building this mosque. But the fatwa is that construction with that yield is permissible. And if the waqf is for repair of the mosque, can the nazir buy a ladder? The sixteenth issue... His statement: (Hisham said... in al-Is'af): If the nazir wants to buy from the mosque waqf oil, mats, bricks, or pebbles to spread, it is permissible if the endower gave broad discretion to the nazir by saying 'do what you see as the interest of the mosque'. If he did not give discretion but rather made the waqf for building and repair only, then he cannot buy what we mentioned because it is not from repair and building. If his condition is not known, one looks...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage contains several distinct rulings on waqf. (1) The nazir may borrow with profit (interest) for urgent repair if no other option, and the increase is his own liability. (2) Building a minaret from mosque waqf is permissible if it serves the interest of making the adhan heard better; otherwise not. (3) If a waqf for mosque repair has surplus that is to go to the poor, the surplus should be saved for future repair needs; only if the accumulated surplus exceeds future needs can it be given to the poor. (4) For a dilapidated mosque, building anew from waqf income is permissible according to fatwa, though al-Khassaf disagreed. (5) The nazir's purchases for the mosque are limited by the endower's stipulation: if broad discretion was given, he may buy items like oil, mats, etc.; if only for building/repair, he cannot; if condition unknown, he must exercise judgment based on interest. The passage ends abruptly at page break. It combines rulings from various sources (al-Qunyah, al-Khaniyah, al-Is'af). Each ruling is a complete legal unit, but here they are presented consecutively.

Key Terms
المنارة (al-manara): Minaret, the tower of a mosque used for adhan.
المصلحة (al-maslahah): Interest or benefit; here, the functional benefit of the minaret.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always
B) When it makes the adhan better heard
C) Only if the endower specified it
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A minaret may be built from waqf income only if it serves a genuine functional need of the mosque.

Surplus Waqf Proceeds: Repair vs. New Building
Ninth and tenth issues: surplus allocation and rebuilding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings on using waqf surplus for future repair needs and for rebuilding a dilapidated mosque.

Core Idea
Surplus waqf income for repair should be saved for future needs; but if a mosque is dilapidated, the fatwa permits rebuilding with the accumulated income.

The ninth and tenth issues address how to handle surplus waqf income designated for repair. If the mosque has not been repaired, the surplus should be withheld for future exigencies. However, if the mosque is already dilapidated and there is enough income to rebuild, the fatwa allows construction despite al-Khassaf's objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ninth issue (surplus)
A waqf stipulates that surplus from repair goes to the poor. The yield accumulates but the mosque does not need repair. Ruling: save the surplus for future needs; if it exceeds future needs, give the balance to the poor.
2
Identify the tenth issue (dilapidation)
A mosque is dilapidated and has enough yield for construction. Al-Khassaf says no (because waqf was for repair, not rebuild). The fatwa says yes.
3
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Al-Khassaf restricts to literal 'repair'; the fatwa takes a broader view that includes rebuilding when necessary.
4
Note the mufta bihi
The fatwa (jumping with the accumulated yield) is the operative position.

Waqf — Endowment

Borrowing at Profit for Waqf Repair
Ruling on borrowing with interest for waqf maintenance when no income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on borrowing with interest for waqf repair and distinguish between waqf liability and personal liability of the custodian.

Core Idea
Borrowing at profit for waqf repair is permitted with the custodian's personal liability, not the waqf's.

When a waqf property urgently needs repair but has no income, and borrowing is only possible with interest (riba), Hanafi law provides a solution. The custodian (qayyim) may borrow at profit, but the extra amount is his personal responsibility. This ruling, from the later Hanafi fatwa work al-Quniyah, balances the preservation of the waqf with the prohibition of riba. The passage also includes a legal stratagem (hila) to avoid direct riba by purchasing an insignificant item from the lender.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem scenario
The waqf has no income and urgently needs repair. A loan is only available with profit (riba). What can the custodian do?
This sets the context of necessity (darurah).
2
Analyze the permissibility of demolition
The custodian must first assess whether demolition is necessary to prevent greater future harm. If so, he may demolish even against local opposition.
The harm principle: preventing greater harm justifies demolition.
3
Examine the borrowing solution
The custodian borrows an amount (e.g., 10 dinars) with an increase (13 dinars) to be repaid in a year. The principal (10) is repaid from waqf income, but the extra (3) is the custodian's personal debt.
The waqf does not bear the riba; it remains on the custodian.
4
Understand the legal stratagem (hila)
To avoid direct riba, the custodian buys something insignificant from the lender for 3 dinars. This transforms the riba into a sale transaction.
This hila is a well-known Hanafi technique to circumvent riba.
5
Recognize the authority and refutation
The ruling is from al-Quniyah, citing Yusuf al-Turjumani al-Saghir. It refutes Ibn Wahban's claim that scholars had no answer.
This is a later fatwa (fatawa mutakhkhirin), not from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : إذا احتاج الوقف إلى العمارة وليس عنده غلة ولم يتيسر القرض إلا بربح. قال في القنية رامزاً ليوسف الترجماني الصغير : قال البصراء للقيم إن لم تهدم المسجد العام يكون ضرره في القابل أعظم فله هدمه وإن خالفه بعض أهل محلته وليس له التأخير إذا أمكنه العمارة، فلو هدمه ولم يكن فيه غلة للعمارة في الحال فاستقرض العشرة بثلاثة عشر في السنة واشترى من المقرض شيئاً يسيراً بثلاثة دنانير يرجع في غلته بالعشرة وعليه الزيادة اهـ. و به اندفع ما ذكره ابن وهبان من أنه لا جواب للمشايخ فيها.
The seventh: If the waqf needs repair and it has no income, and a loan is not available except with profit. It is stated in al-Quniyah, referring to Yusuf al-Turjumani al-Saghir: The knowledgeable ones said to the custodian: If you do not demolish the mosque this year, its harm will be greater in the future, so he may demolish it even if some residents of the neighborhood oppose him, and he may not delay if repair is possible. If he demolishes it and there is no income for repair immediately, then he borrows ten with thirteen per year and buys from the lender something insignificant for three dinars; he recovers from its income the ten, and the excess is upon him. By this is refuted what Ibn Wahban mentioned that there is no answer from the scholars on this.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This is a ruling on waqf repair from the book al-Quniyah. When a waqf property like a mosque is in urgent need of repair but has no income, and borrowing is only possible with interest (riba), the custodian (qayyim) is permitted to demolish the structure to prevent greater future harm, even against local opposition. For immediate repair costs, he may borrow money at a profit (e.g., borrow 10 with 13 to be repaid in a year). To avoid direct interest, he purchases a small item from the lender for 3 dinars, making the transaction a sale. The principal (10) is repaid from waqf income, but the extra (3) is the custodian's personal liability, not the waqf's. This follows the Hanafi principle that interest cannot be charged to the waqf, but the custodian may bear it. The ruling addresses the practical difficulty of waqf maintenance.

Key Terms
قيم (qayyim): The custodian or manager of a waqf property.
قرض (qard): A loan that must be repaid, often with an increase (riba), which is normally prohibited but allowed here for necessity.
غلة (ghallah): Income or revenue generated by the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the extra amount (interest) handled when a custodian borrows for waqf repair?
A) It is repaid from the waqf's income.
B) It is forgiven by the lender.
C) It becomes the personal debt of the custodian.
D) It is paid from a special waqf fund.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits borrowing at profit for waqf repair when necessary, provided the interest is a personal liability of the custodian, not the waqf.

Building a Minaret from Waqf Income: The Condition of Need
Ruling on building a minaret from waqf income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition for using waqf funds on a mosque minaret: permissible only if it improves audibility of the adhan.

Core Idea
Waqf funds for minaret: only if it makes the adhan more audible; unnecessary spending is not allowed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical question every mosque committee faces: can a mosque's waqf income be used to build a minaret? The Hanafi scholar Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, as recorded in al-Khaniyyah, provides a conditional ruling. It teaches us that waqf money must be spent only on genuine needs, not on superfluous additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
Recognize that the passage asks whether it is permissible to build a minaret from the mosque's waqf income (ghullah).
2
Locate the condition for permissibility
The passage states it is permissible if the minaret brings benefit (maslahah) to the mosque, specifically by making the adhan more audible.
The benefit here is acoustical, not aesthetic.
3
Apply the converse condition
If the adhan is already clearly heard by the neighbors without a minaret, then building it is not allowed, as it constitutes wasteful spending of waqf resources.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that waqf funds must be used for essential or truly beneficial purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامنة في وقف المسجد : أيجوز أن يبنى من غلته منارة؟ قال في الخانية معزياً إلى أبي بكر البلخي : إن كان ذلك من مصلحة المسجد بأن كان أسمع لهم فلا بأس به، وإن كان بحال يسمع الجيران الأذان بغير منارة فلا أرى لهم أن يفعلوا ذلك
The eighth: Regarding the endowment of a mosque: Is it permissible to build a minaret from its income? It is said in al-Khaniyyah, attributed to Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: If that is for the benefit of the mosque, such that it makes the call to prayer more audible, then there is no harm in it. But if the neighbors can hear the adhan without a minaret, then I do not think they should do that.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This is a ruling about using the income of a mosque's waqf to build a minaret. The Hanafi scholar Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, as reported in al-Khaniyyah, conditions permissibility on benefit: if the minaret makes the adhan louder and more useful, it may be built from waqf funds. If the adhan is already clearly heard without it, building a minaret would be unnecessary and thus not allowed, as it wastes waqf money. This reflects the Hanafi principle that waqf income must be spent only on genuine needs of the mosque.

Key Terms
منارة (manarah): A minaret; a structure from which the adhan is called.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is building a minaret from mosque waqf income allowed?
A) Only if the imam requests it.
B) If it makes the adhan more audible; otherwise not.
C) Whenever the custodian wishes.
D) If it is made of stone, not wood.

Key Takeaway
Building a minaret from mosque waqf income is permissible only if it improves the audibility of the adhan; otherwise it is not allowed.

Distribution of Surplus Waqf Income After Repairs
Intra-Hanafi ruling on surplus waqf income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi positions on surplus waqf income and apply the preferred view to a given waqf scenario.

Core Idea
Surplus waqf income is saved for future repairs before distributing to the poor.

Waqf properties often generate income that exceeds immediate repair needs. When a waqf is established with the condition that surplus after repair goes to the poor, how should the custodian act when there is no current need? Hanafi jurists differed on whether to save all income for future emergencies or distribute the surplus. This lesson explores these views and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqf condition
The waqf is for mosque repair, with any surplus after repair going to the poor. Income (ghallah) accumulates while the mosque is not in need of repair.
The condition explicitly ties distribution to the state of repair needs.
2
Understand Abu Bakr's position
Faqih Abu Bakr argued that all income should be withheld because a future accident might occur or the land might cease to yield income. He prioritizes precaution.
This is the most conservative view.
3
Analyze Abu Ja'far's refinement
Abu Ja'far agreed with Abu Bakr in principle but added: if the accumulated income is enough for likely future repairs, the surplus may be given to the poor as per the waqf condition.
He introduces a threshold of sufficiency.
4
Note Abu al-Layth's preferred view
Abu al-Layth adopts the same approach as Abu Ja'far: consider whether the income suffices for future repairs; if so, distribute the surplus. This is declared sahih (sound) in al-Khaniyyah.
This becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
5
Apply the prohibition on loans
Al-Quniyah clarifies that the custodian cannot take the surplus as a loan (debt) to give to the poor now and recover from future shares. The surplus must be genuinely excess after securing future repairs.
This prevents misuse of waqf funds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسعة : وقف على عمارة المسجد على أن ما فضل من عمارته فهو للفقراء فاجتمعت الغلة والمسجد غير محتاج إلى العمارة قال الفقيه أبو بكر : تحبس الغلة لأنه ربما يحدث بالمسجد حدث وتصير الأرض بحال لا تغل. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : الجواب كما قال، وعندي لو علم أنه لو اجتمع من الغلة مقدار ما يحتاج الأرض والمسجد إلى العمارة يمكن العمارة بها ويفضل تصرف الزيادة إلى الفقراء على ما شرط الواقف. وفي القنية : ليس للقيم أن يأخذ ما فضل من وجه عمارة المدرسة ديناً ليصرفها إلى الفقراء وإن احتاجوا إليه . وفي الخانية والصحيح ما قال الفقيه أبو الليث أنه ينظر إن اجتمع الغلة مقدار ما لو احتاج الضيعة والمسجد إلى العمارة بعد ذلك يمكن العمارة منها ويبقى شيء تصرف تلك الزيادة إلى الفقراء .اهـ. ريع غلة الوقف للعمارة وثلاثة أرباعها للفقراء لم يجز للقيم أن يصرف ريع العمارة إذا استغنى عنها إلى الفقراء ليسترد ذلك من حصتهم في السنة الثانية اهـ.
The ninth: A waqf for the repair of a mosque on condition that whatever remains from its repair is for the poor. Income accumulates while the mosque has no need for repair. Faqih Abu Bakr said: The income should be withheld, because perhaps an accident may occur to the mosque and the land may become such that it yields no income. Faqih Abu Ja'far said: The answer is as he said, but in my view, if one knows that the income has accumulated enough for the future needs of the land and mosque, then the surplus may be given to the poor as the waqf specified. In al-Quniyah: The custodian may not take the surplus from the repair of a madrasa as a loan to give to the poor, even if they need it. In al-Khaniyyah, the correct is what Faqih Abu al-Layth said: It is considered: if the income has accumulated such that if the estate and mosque need repair later, it can be done and something remains, that surplus is given to the poor. The produce of waqf income for repair and three-quarters for the poor: the custodian may not spend the repair income if it is not needed, to recover that from their share in the second year.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about surplus waqf income designated for mosque repair and then for the poor. Three positions: 1) Abu Bakr: All income is saved for future emergencies; 2) Abu Ja'far: If enough for likely future repairs, surplus goes to poor; 3) Abu al-Layth (preferred): Similar to Abu Ja'far: if surplus remains after setting aside for future repairs, distribute. Also, the custodian cannot treat surplus as a loan to give to the poor and then recoup from future shares. The Hanafi ruling favors preserving the waqf's purpose before distributing to beneficiaries.

Key Terms
غلة (ghallah): Income or yield from waqf property.
مرمة (marammah): Repair and maintenance of waqf property.
قيم (qayyim): Custodian or manager of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Khaniyyah, when may surplus waqf income designated for repair be given to the poor?
A) Immediately, regardless of future needs.
B) Only after the waqf property ceases to generate income.
C) When enough income has been set aside for likely future repairs.
D) Only with the permission of the local judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preferred view balances waqf sustainability and beneficiary rights: surplus may be distributed only after securing a reserve for future repairs.

Rebuilding a Ruined Mosque from Waqf Income
Ruling on using waqf repair funds for complete rebuilding, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi fatwa on using waqf repair income for complete rebuilding and identify the intra-madhhab difference between al-Khassaf and the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Waqf income for repair can fund rebuilding – al-Khassaf's restriction is overruled by the fatwa.

When a mosque is completely ruined, its waqf may have accumulated enough income originally intended for repairs. Can the custodian use that income for a full rebuild? Al-Khassaf argued no, because the donor specified 'repair', not 'construction'. But the later Hanafi fatwa says yes: rebuilding is the ultimate repair. This lesson examines that dispute and its practical consequence for waqf management.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and its ruling
The text describes a mosque that is ruined (tahaddama) and has collected sufficient income from its waqf (ghallah) to enable construction. The core question: can that income be spent on rebuilding?
Note the distinction between 'marammah' (repair) and 'bina' (construction).
2
State al-Khassaf's position and his proof
Al-Khassaf said: the income should NOT be spent on construction because the waqf was made for repair, not for building. His proof is the donor's expressed intention – the waqf was restricted to repair.
Al-Khassaf's view represents a strict adherence to the textual condition of the waqf.
3
State the fatwa position and its basis
The text then says 'wal-fatwa ala annahu yajuz' – the fatwa is that it IS permissible to build with that income. The basis is that rebuilding a completely ruined mosque is itself a form of repair; the repair fund can cover it.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
4
Understand the legal reasoning behind the tarjih
The fatwa expands the meaning of 'marammah' to include total reconstruction when the mosque is beyond repair. This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas that would restrict funds.
Al-Khassaf's view is a minority within the Hanafi school; the later authorities preferred the more flexible view.
5
Consider the transition to sub-issue (ladder etc.)
The text then mentions a separate sub-issue: buying a ladder, oil, mats, etc. for the mosque. This depends on the waqf's terms: if broad discretion given, it's allowed; if restricted to 'building and repair', then not; if unknown, the custodian should investigate.
This sub-issue illustrates the same tension: what counts as 'repair' vs. 'improvement'?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العاشرة : مسجد تهدم وقد اجتمع من غلته ما يحصل به البناء قال الخصاف : لا ينفق الغلة في البناء لأن الواقف وقف على مرمتها ولم يأمر بأن يبنى هذا المسجد، والفتوى على أنه يجوز البناء بتلك الغلة. ولو كان الوقف على عمارة المسجد هل للقيم أن يشتري سلماً؟ المسألة السادسة عشرة. قوله : (قال هشام الخ في الإسعاف ولو أراد المتولي أن يشتري من وقف المسجد دهناً أو حصراً أو أجراً أو حصى ليفرش فيه يجوز إن وسع الواقف في ذلك للقيم بأن قال يفعل ما يراه من مصلحة المسجد، وإن لم يوسع بل وقفه لبناء المسجد وعمارته فليس له أن يشتري ما ذكرنا لأنه ليس من العمارة والبناء. وإن لم يعرف شرطه في ذلك ينظر هذا القيم إلى من
The tenth: A mosque is ruined, and from its income has collected enough for construction. Al-Khassaf said: The income should not be spent on construction, because the waqf was made for its repair, and the waqf did not order the building of this mosque. But the fatwa is that it is permissible to build with that income. And if the waqf was for the repair of the mosque, does the custodian have the right to buy a ladder? The sixteenth issue. His saying: (Hisham said) in al-Is'af: If the administrator wants to buy from the mosque's waqf oil, mats, bricks, or gravel to spread in it, it is allowed if the waqf allowed that to the custodian by saying 'do what you see as the mosque's interest'. But if he did not allow, but rather made waqf for building and repair, then he may not buy what we mentioned because it is not from repair and building. And if his condition is not known, then the custodian looks to whoever...
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage deals with a ruined mosque that has enough accumulated income to rebuild. Al-Khassaf (a Hanafi scholar) argued that waqf income designated for repair (marammah) cannot be used for complete rebuilding because the waqf specified repair, not new construction. However, the later fatwa (mufta bihi) permits rebuilding from that income, as it is essentially a greater repair. Then it transitions to a separate sub-issue (السادسة عشرة): whether the custodian can buy items like oil or mats if the waqf did not specify them. Hisham's report in al-Is'af says: if the waqf gave broad discretion, it's allowed; if restricted to building and repair, then not; if condition unknown, the custodian must seek guidance. The text is cut off on the page.

Key Terms
مرمة (marammah): Repair; minor maintenance as opposed to complete rebuilding.
بناء (bina): Construction; building anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using accumulated waqf income to rebuild a completely ruined mosque according to the text?
A) It is not allowed according to al-Khassaf and the fatwa.
B) It is allowed only if the waqf specifies 'bina'.
C) Al-Khassaf said no, but the fatwa says yes.
D) It is allowed only with qadi's permission.

Key Takeaway
Rebuilding a ruined mosque is permissible using waqf repair income, according to the Hanafi fatwa, despite al-Khassaf's objection.

Repairing a Shared Wall Between Waqf and Private Property
Ruling on repair of shared wall between waqf and private shops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repairing a shared wall between waqf and private property and explain the conditions under which the waqf custodian may borrow for repairs.

Core Idea
A waqf's leaning wall must be repaired from its income; if none, borrowing requires the qadi's authorization.

This lesson examines a specific case from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: when a waqf-owned shop shares a wall with private shops and the wall leans. The ruling clarifies the custodian's duty and the limits of his authority. Understanding this helps you grasp the Hanafi approach to waqf maintenance and the protective role of the qadi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
Recognize that there are multiple shops: the first is waqf, the rest are privately owned. They share a wall that is leaning and in danger of collapse.
The wall is part of the waqf property.
2
Determine the ruling when waqf has income
If the waqf has income (ghallah), the custodian must use that income to repair the wall. The private owners can compel him to do so.
Repair is wajib to prevent harm.
3
Determine the ruling when waqf has no income
If the waqf has no income, the private owners raise the matter to the qadi. The qadi orders the custodian to borrow money on behalf of the waqf for the repair.
Borrowing is permitted only with qadi's order.
4
Note the condition: no independent borrowing
The custodian cannot borrow without the qadi's permission. This protects the waqf's assets from unauthorized debt.
The text explicitly says: 'and he may not borrow without the qadi's order'.
5
Identify the authority
This ruling is cited from al-Khaniyyah, a later Hanafi fatwa collection (fatawa mutakhkhirin), indicating its reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادية عشرة : حوانيت مال بعضها إلى بعض والأول منها وقف والباقي ملك والمتولي لا الوقف قال أبو قاسم إن كان للوقف غلة كان لأصحاب يعمر الحوانيت أن يأخذوا القيم ليسوي الحائط المائل من غلة الوقف وإن لم يكن للوقف غلة في يد القيم رفعوا الأمر إلى القاضي ليأمر القاضي القيم بالاستدانة على الوقف في إصلاح الوقف، وليس له أن يستدين بغير أمر القاضي؛ كذا في الخانية
The eleventh: Shops adjoining each other, the first of them is waqf and the rest are privately owned, and the administrator is not for the waqf. Abu Qasim said: If the waqf has income, the owners of the shops to be built can take the custodian to straighten the leaning wall from the waqf's income. But if there is no income in the custodian's hand, they raise the matter to the qadi so that the qadi orders the custodian to borrow on behalf of the waqf for its repair. And he may not borrow without the qadi's order. As in al-Khaniyyah.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This ruling deals with a shared wall between a waqf shop and privately owned shops. The wall leans and needs repair. If the waqf has income, the private owners can compel the waqf custodian to spend from that income to fix the wall, as it is a necessary repair for the waqf property. If the waqf has no income, the matter goes to the qadi, who can authorize the custodian to borrow money for the repair on the waqf's credit. The custodian cannot borrow independently; qadi's permission is required to protect the waqf's assets.

Key Terms
حائط مائل (ha'it ma'il): A leaning wall that is in danger of collapse.
استدانة (istidanah): Borrowing money for waqf repair under qadi's authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a waqf leaning wall needs repair, the custodian must use waqf income if available; if not, he may only borrow with the qadi's explicit permission.
