Prioritizing Waqf Expenses Over Beneficiaries
Ruling on waqf expense priority and custodian actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the principle that waqf expenses must be covered from income before distributing to beneficiaries, and APPLY this rule to scenarios involving repairs, replanting, and building decisions.

Core Idea
Waqf income first covers expenses; only the surplus is for beneficiaries.

When a waqf is established for the poor without specifying repairs, the custodian must ensure the property's sustainability. This ruling establishes that necessary expenses—such as maintenance, land tax, and preservation costs—must be paid from the income before any distribution. The text then expands to cover practical scenarios where the custodian may take proactive steps to prevent loss and maximize benefit, always prioritizing the waqf's long-term viability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default priority rule
The custodian must begin with expenditures for repair and maintenance ('imarah) from the waqf revenue before distributing anything to beneficiaries.
This is the foundational principle: preservation of the waqf property comes first.
2
List the deductible expenses
Expenses include repair costs, land tax (kharaj), and other necessary expenses (mu'un). All must be paid from the income.
The text explicitly mentions kharaj as a priority expense.
3
Apply to specific cases of preservation
The custodian may replant date palms if old ones are dying, improve salty soil, build housing for workers, and hire a caretaker. Each action is permitted because it preserves the waqf.
These actions are considered part of 'imarah (maintenance/improvement).
4
Determine the exception for building rental houses
Building houses for rent is generally prohibited on agricultural waqf land, but permitted if the land adjoins urban areas and renting yields higher profit, as it is more beneficial for the poor.
The principle of maximizing benefit (manfa'ah) overrides the general rule.
5
Summarize the underlying principle
All custodian actions must aim to preserve the waqf and maximize its benefit for the beneficiaries, without fundamentally altering the waqf's purpose.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) in waqf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية عشرة: لو وقف على المساكين ولم يذكر العمارة يبدأ من الغلة بالعمارة وبما يصلحها وبخراجها ومؤنها ثم يقسم الباقي على المساكين، فإن كان في الأرض نخل ويخاف القيم هلاكها كان للقيم أن يشتري من الوقف فسيلاً فيغرسه كيلا ينقطع، فلو كانت قطعة منها سبخة تحتاج إلى رفع وجهها وإصلاحها حتى تنبت كان للقيم أن يبدأ من جملة غلة الأرض في ذلك ويصلح القطعة، أراد القيم أن يبني في الأرض الموقوفة قرية لأكرتها وحفاظها ليحفظ فيها الغلة ويجمعها كان له أن يفعل ذلك، وكذا لو كان الوقف خاناً على الفقراء واحتاج إلى خادم يكسح الخان ويقوم به ويفتح بابه ويسده فسلم بعض البيوت إلى رجل أجرة له ليقوم بذلك كان له ذلك، وإن أراد قيم الوقف أن يبني في الأرض الموقوفة بيوتاً يستغلها بالإجارة لا يكون له ذلك لأن استغلال أرض الوقف يكون بالزرع، ولو كانت الأرض متصلة ببيوت المصر يرغب الناس في استئجار بيوتها وتكون غلة ذلك فوق غلة الزرع والنخل كان للقيم أن يبني فيها بيوتاً فيؤاجرها لأن الاستغلال بهذا الوجه يكون أنفع للفقراء؛ كذا في الخانية.
The twelfth: If one makes a waqf for the poor and does not mention repair, one begins from the income with repair, with what is needed for its maintenance, its land tax, and its expenses, then divides the remainder among the poor. If there are date palms in the land and the custodian fears their destruction, he may buy from the waqf offshoots and plant them so they do not die out. If there is a plot that is salty, needing its level raised and improvement so that it grows, the custodian may start from the total income of the land for that and improve the plot. If the custodian wants to build in the waqf land a village for its tenants and guards to preserve and collect the produce, he may do that. Likewise, if the waqf is a caravanserai for the poor and needs a servant to sweep it, maintain it, open and close its door, and he gives some rooms to a man as his wage to do that, he may do so. But if the custodian wants to build houses in the waqf land to lease them, he may not do that because the exploitation of waqf land is through cultivation. However, if the land adjoins urban houses and people desire to rent its houses and its income is greater than from cultivation and palm trees, then the custodian may build houses and lease them because that exploitation is more beneficial for the poor. As in al-Khaniyyah.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This ruling covers multiple scenarios regarding waqf land given for the poor without specifying repairs. The default principle: before distributing income to beneficiaries, the custodian must deduct repair costs, land tax, and other necessary expenses. This includes preventing loss of date palms by replanting, improving salty soil, building worker housing, and hiring a caretaker for a caravanserai. However, building houses for rent is generally not allowed if the land is agricultural, because the purpose of agricultural waqf is farming. But an exception is made if the land is in a city area where renting houses yields more profit; then building is permitted as it benefits the poor more. This shows Hanafi flexibility to maximize waqf benefit while respecting the waqf's original purpose.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land.
فسيل (fasil): A young offshoot of a date palm used for replanting.
غلة (ghallah): Income or produce from waqf property.
عمارة (imarah): Repair and maintenance of the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a waqf custodian wants to build houses for rent on agricultural waqf land, when is it allowed?
A) Always allowed, because the custodian can decide.
B) Only allowed if the land adjoins urban areas and rental income exceeds agricultural income.
C) Never allowed, because waqf land must remain agricultural.
D) Allowed only with permission from all beneficiaries.

Key Takeaway
Waqf income must first cover all necessary expenses; only the remainder is distributed to beneficiaries, and the custodian may take actions to preserve and maximize benefit within the waqf's purpose.

Leasing Part of Waqf for Its Maintenance
Ruling on leasing waqf for repair with proof from Imam Muhammad and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing part of a waqf for its repair and apply qiyas to similar cases like a mosque roof.

Core Idea
Leasing part of a waqf for essential maintenance is permissible by textual narration and analogy.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical challenge: how to fund repairs of a waqf property without selling it. Imam Muhammad provides two narrated solutions for a caravanserai, and Al-Natif extends the reasoning to a mosque by qiyas. We will examine the proofs and the analogical reasoning, a hallmark of Hanafi flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
A waqf property (caravanserai) needs repair but lacks funds; the question is how to generate revenue without violating the inalienability of waqf.
2
Extract the two narrated opinions
From Imam Muhammad: (1) separate and lease one or two rooms for repair funds; (2) lease the entire property for a fixed term and use proceeds for repair.
These are two valid riwayat within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The narration itself is the textual basis; it explicitly permits leasing for maintenance. Consider its transmission (zanni) and clarity (qati dalala).
The proof is from a Hanafi imam, not from Quran or Sunnah directly.
4
Understand the qiyas to the mosque
Al-Natif reasons that the ruling on the caravanserai applies to a mosque roof because both are waqf properties needing repair and lacking funds. The illa (effective cause) is the need for maintenance and unavailability of other funds.
This is a clear example of tahqiq al-manat: verifying the illa.
5
Note the conditions and limitations
The permissibility is conditional: (i) genuine need for repair, (ii) no other funds, (iii) leasing does not permanently alter the waqf's purpose. Not a general license to lease waqf for profit.
These conditions are implicit in the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة عشرة: لو وخاناً واحتاج إلى المرمة روي عن محمد أنه يعزل منه بيت أو بيتان فتؤاجر وينفق من غلتها عليه، وعنه رواية أخرى إجارة الكل سنة ويسترم منها . قال الناطفي: قياسه في المسجد أن يجوز إجارة سطحه لمرمته ؛ كذا في الظهيرية
The thirteenth: If there is a caravanserai [waqf] and it needs repair, it is narrated from Muhammad that one separates one or two rooms from it, leases them, and spends from their income on its repair. From him is another narration: lease the whole for a year and use [the proceeds] for its repair. Al-Natif said: Its analogy for a mosque is that it is permissible to lease its roof for its repair. As in al-Zahirah.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This ruling offers two narrated opinions from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on how to fund repairs of a waqf caravanserai: either lease a portion (one or two rooms) and use that rent for maintenance, or lease the entire property for a fixed term and use the rent. Al-Natif extends the analogy to a mosque: leasing its roof for advertisements or similar to generate repair funds is permissible by qiyas. This shows Hanafi permissibility of using waqf assets temporarily to generate income for essential maintenance, as long as the waqf's primary purpose is not permanently altered.

Key Terms
مرمة (marammah): Repair of a waqf property.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here extending ruling from caravanserai to mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Natif analogize to permit leasing a mosque's roof for repair?
A) Leasing a room in a waqf caravanserai.
B) Selling waqf property.
C) Borrowing with interest.
D) Giving charity from waqf income.

Key Takeaway
Leasing part of a waqf for essential repairs is permitted by Hanafi jurists based on narrations from Imam Muhammad and analogical reasoning.

Selling a Waqf Tree for Repairs: The Prohibition and the Correct Method
Ruling on selling a waqf tree to fund repair of waqf house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a component of waqf to fund repairs and identify the correct alternative method.

Core Idea
You cannot sell part of a waqf to repair the rest; instead, rent the property and use the rent.

This passage from Fatawa Samarqand addresses a practical dilemma: a waqf house has a tree, and the house is ruined. Can the mutawalli sell the tree to fix the house? The answer is no, because the tree is also waqf. The correct procedure is to rent the house (even if partially usable) and use the rental income for repairs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a waqf tree to repair a waqf house. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram).
2
Identify the correct alternative
The mutawalli should rent the house and use the rental income for repairs, not sell the tree.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Waqf assets must be preserved intact; selling is only permitted under extreme need with qadi's permission, not for routine maintenance.
4
Note the source authority
This ruling is from Fatawa Samarqand and endorsed by al-Zahirah, representing later Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة عشرة في فتاوى سمرقند شجرة وقف في دار وقف خربت ليس للمتولي أن يبيع الشجرة ويعمر الدار ولكن يكري الدار ويستعين بالكراء على عمارة الدار لا بالشجرة؛ كذا في الظهيرية
The fourteenth: In the Fatawa of Samarqand: A waqf tree in a waqf house that has become ruined. The administrator may not sell the tree and repair the house with its price. Rather, he rents the house and uses the rent to repair the house, not the tree. As in al-Zahirah.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that individual components of a waqf (like a tree) cannot be sold to fund repairs of the waqf property itself, because the tree is part of the waqf and cannot be sold. The proper method is to rent out the house (even if ruined, perhaps for some use) and use that rent to fund repairs. This preserves the waqf's assets intact while generating income for maintenance.

Key Terms
متولي (mutawalli): Administrator of a waqf; same as qayyim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sell the tree and use proceeds for repair.
B) Rent the house and use rent for repair.
C) Sell both the tree and house.
D) Abandon the property.

Key Takeaway
A waqf asset cannot be sold to fund repairs of the waqf itself; rental income must be used.

Eating from Waqf Produce: Custodian's Rights and Dispute
Ruling on waqf custodian's personal use of produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling for a waqf custodian eating from waqf produce and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding purchasing goods at inflated prices for waqf repair.

Core Idea
The waqf custodian may not eat from waqf produce unless the waqf stipulates it; disputed is whether he may buy goods above value for repair.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq examines whether a waqf administrator may personally benefit from waqf income. The default ruling is clear: no personal consumption without authorization. However, a related issue emerges: can the administrator buy overpriced goods to generate profit for the waqf? The text presents two conflicting Hanafi opinions, requiring careful analysis of the underlying legal principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Read the opening question: 'hal yajuz al-akl min ghallat al-waqf?' The implied answer from al-Ramli's words is that it is not permissible unless one buys from the produce in a manner previously described.
The default position is prohibition for personal use.
2
Recognize the expansion
The text shifts to a related scenario from al-Ashbah: whether the administrator can buy goods at an inflated price to sell later, using the profit for repairs, with any loss on the waqf.
This expansion probes the limits of the custodian's authority to benefit the waqf through trade.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Ibn Wahban permits this practice, while al-Maqdisi refutes it citing al-Quniyah. The commentary attempts to reconcile the views by pointing to the presence or absence of a binding term (ajal) in the transaction.
The dispute centers on whether the transaction harms the waqf or serves its interest.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
If there is no binding term (as in a loan with grace), buying a small item at a high price is pure harm, so the increase is on the custodian. If there is a binding term, the loss may be absorbed by the waqf as part of a trade strategy.
The distinction is based on necessity and benefit to the waqf.
5
Apply the ruling
The default prohibition stands unless the waqf founder explicitly allows consumption or the transaction meets strict conditions of benefit and absence of exploitation.
Modern analog: a trustee cannot take a salary from trust assets without authorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة عشرة: هل يجوز الأكل من غلة الوقف؟ قال الرملي: قال كان قبله فإن كان يشتري من الغلة ما ذكرنا جاز له الشراء وإلا فلا .اهـ قوله : (وعليه الزيادة) قال في الأشباه : وهل يجوز للمتولي أن يشتري متاعاً بأكثر من قيمته ويبيعه ويصرفه على العمارة ويكون الربح على الوقف؟ الجواب : نعم كما حرره ابن وهبان اهـ. أقول: بينهما ما يشبه المخالفة إلا أن يقال : لما لم يلزم الأجل في مسألة القرض بقي مجرد شراء اليسير بثمن كثير فتمحض ضرراً على الوقف فلم تلزمه الزيادة فكانت على القيم بخلاف مسألة شراء المتاع وبيعه للزوم الأجل في جملة الثمن فتأمل اهـ. لكن قال المقدسي : إن ما في القنية يرد ما قاله ابن وهبان. قوله: (فسيلاً)
The fifteenth: Is it permissible to eat from the produce of the waqf? Al-Ramli said: He said before him: if he buys from the produce what we mentioned, then purchase is allowed for him, otherwise not. His saying: (And the increase is upon him) is stated in al-Ashbah: Is it permissible for the administrator to buy goods for more than their value and sell them and spend on repair, with the profit being for the waqf? The answer: Yes, as compiled by Ibn Wahban. I say: Between them there is something resembling contradiction, except that it is said: Since there was no binding term in the loan issue, the mere purchase of a small thing for a large price became pure harm to the waqf, so the increase does not bind the waqf; it is on the custodian. Unlike the issue of buying goods and selling them due to the binding term in the total price. Reflect. But al-Maqdisi said: What is in al-Quniyah refutes what Ibn Wahban said. His saying: (an offshoot).
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This lesson addresses whether the waqf custodian may personally benefit from waqf produce (e.g., eating from it). The ruling appears to be that he may not, unless the waqf allows it. The text then digresses into a related issue from al-Ashbah about buying goods at inflated prices to raise funds for repair, with profit to waqf. There is a scholarly difference: Ibn Wahban permits it, but al-Maqdisi says al-Quniyah contradicts that. The final phrase 'his saying: (an offshoot)' refers back to an earlier marginal note. The passage is textually messy; the core ruling is that the custodian cannot eat from waqf produce without explicit authorization.

Key Terms
غلة (ghallah): Produce or income of waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the beginning of this passage, can the custodian eat from the waqf's produce?
A) Yes, if he works for the waqf.
B) No, unless the waqf stipulates it.
C) Yes, always.
D) Only with the qadi's permission.

Key Takeaway
The default is that the waqf custodian may not personally consume waqf produce without explicit authorization from the founder.

Spending Mosque Endowment Income on Maintenance
States permissibility of using mosque endowment income for cleaning and snow removal under condition of preventing ruin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on spending mosque endowment income for maintenance and identify the condition that makes such expenditure permissible.

Core Idea
Preventing ruin justifies spending waqf income on maintenance not explicitly stipulated.

Mosque endowments are established to ensure the continuous use of the mosque. But what about expenses not mentioned in the endowment deed, like sweeping roofs or removing snow? This lesson from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi position, balancing the donor's terms with the essential goal of preserving the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is spending the mosque's endowment income (ghallah) on maintenance tasks such as sweeping the roof, removing snow, and clearing debris. The ruling is that it is permissible (yajuz/mubah).
2
Locate the condition
The permissibility is conditional: the expenditure must be necessary to prevent the mosque from falling into ruin (kharab). If the task can be neglected without causing ruin, it is not automatically allowed.
The passage states: 'that which if abandoned would cause ruin of the mosque'.
3
Understand the rationale
The purpose of a mosque waqf is to preserve the mosque for worship. Preventing ruin is a primary objective that overrides strict adherence to the donor's explicit terms.
4
Identify the source authority
The ruling is attributed to Abu Nasr (a Hanafi jurist) and is recorded in al-Khaniyya, a nawadir (non-core) Hanafi text. This authority gives the ruling weight despite not being from the most authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلة ولو ليرتقي على السطح لكنس السطح وتطيينه أو يعطى من غلة المسجد أجر من يكنس السطح ويطرح الثلج ويخرج التراب المجتمع من المسجد ؟ قال أبو نصر للقيم أن يفعل ما في تركه خراب المسجد؛ كذا في الخانية.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the permissible expenditure of a mosque's endowment (waqf) income. The issue is whether the custodian (qayyim) may use the mosque's revenue—typically dedicated to the mosque's upkeep—to pay workers for specific maintenance tasks like sweeping the roof, removing snow, and clearing debris. Abu Nasr (a Hanafi jurist) rules that the custodian is permitted to do whatever is necessary to prevent the mosque from falling into ruin. This is based on the general principle that the purpose of a mosque waqf is the preservation and upkeeping of the mosque, and preventing ruin is a primary objective. The ruling is taken from the Hanafi work al-Khaniyya.

Key Terms

Two Narrations from Imam Muhammad on Funding Waqf Repairs
Presents two narrations from Imam Muhammad on funding waqf repairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Imam Muhammad regarding funding waqf repairs and identify the common principle that the corpus must not be sold.

Core Idea
When a waqf needs repair, lease part or all of it — never sell the corpus.

A waqf is an endowment whose corpus must be preserved. When repairs are needed but funds are lacking, the custodian (mutawalli) cannot sell the property. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani transmitted two methods to generate repair funds by leasing. This lesson examines both narrations and their extension to mosques via qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The waqf property is in need of repair (marammah) but has no available funds. The corpus cannot be sold or consumed.
2
First narration: lease part
Imam Muhammad: set aside one or two rooms (or units) and lease them; use the rent exclusively for repairs.
This preserves the rest of the waqf for its original purpose.
3
Second narration: lease all
Another narration: lease the entire property for one year and use all rental income for repairs.
This may generate more funds but temporarily changes use.
4
Qiyas to mosque roof
Al-Natifi extends the same principle to mosques: leasing the roof is permissible to fund mosque repairs.
The roof is not essential for prayer and can be leased.
5
Determine the operative ruling
Both narrations are part of Zahir al-Riwayah and accepted. The mutawalli may choose either method based on practicality.
No tarjih (preference) is given; both are mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة عشرة: لو واحتاج إلى المرمة روي عن محمد أنه يعزل منه بيت أو بيتان فتؤاجر وينفق من غلتها عليه، وعنه رواية أخرى إجارة الكل سنة ويسترم منها . قال الناطفي: قياسه في المسجد أن يجوز إجارة سطحه لمرمته ؛ كذا في الظهيرية
The thirteenth [issue]: If [a waqf] needs repair, it is narrated from Muhammad that he sets aside one or two rooms from it, which are leased and [the rent] is spent on its repair. And from him is another narration: leasing all of it for a year and repairing from that [rent]. Al-Natifi said: By analogy, for a mosque it is permissible to lease its roof for its repair; thus in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the method of funding repairs for a waqf property that has become dilapidated. Two narrations exist: (1) The custodian should isolate one or two rooms (or units) of the waqf, lease them out, and use that rent exclusively for repairs. (2) Alternatively, lease the entire property for one year and use the entire rental income for repairs. Both methods aim to generate funds for restoration without selling the waqf. Al-Natifi extends this qiyas (analogy) to a mosque: leasing its roof to generate funds for its repair is permissible. The source is al-Zahiriyya. The existence of two narrations indicates that both are accepted within the school, and the custodian may choose based on what is more practical.

Key Terms
مرمة (marammah): The need for repair or restoration of a waqf property.
إجارة السطح (ijārat al-sath): Leasing the roof of a mosque, e.g., for advertisements or as a space, to generate repair funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) By setting aside one or two rooms to lease for repair expenses.
C) By borrowing from the bank.
D) By appealing for donations.

Key Takeaway
For waqf repair, the Hanafi school permits leasing part or all of the property to generate repair funds, preserving the corpus.

Selling a Waqf Tree for Repairs: Prohibition
A short fatwa prohibiting sale of waqf tree for repairs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a part of a waqf corpus and identify the permissible alternative for funding repairs.

Core Idea
The waqf corpus is inviolable – no part, not even a tree, can be sold.

This brief fatwa from Samarqand addresses a practical dilemma: a waqf house is dilapidated and contains a tree that is part of the endowment. The custodian might be tempted to sell the tree to fund repairs. The Hanafi ruling firmly blocks this path, emphasizing the inviolability of the waqf corpus. Instead, rental income from the house itself must be used. Let us examine the legal reasoning behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? The act is: selling a tree that belongs to the waqf (shajarat waqf) to obtain funds to repair the waqf house. The ruling: this is prohibited (haram).
The prohibition applies even for a seemingly beneficial purpose like repair.
2
Identify the Permissible Alternative
The text gives a clear alternative: rent out the house (yukrī al-dār) and use the rental income for repairs. Renting does not alter the corpus.
Rental income is a product (ghalla) of the waqf, not the corpus itself.
3
Extract the Underlying Legal Principle
The principle is that the waqf corpus (al-'ayn al-mawquf) cannot be sold or alienated. This includes trees, buildings, and all physical assets. The custodian (mutawallī) is only a manager, not an owner.
This principle is rooted in the permanence (ta'bid) of waqf.
4
Apply to Similar Scenarios
Consider if a waqf wall collapses: can the custodian sell bricks or timber from another part of the waqf to rebuild? The same rule applies: sell even a part is prohibited; use rental income or donations.
The illa (effective cause) is the inviolability of the corpus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة عشرة في فتاوى سمرقند شجرة وقف في دار وقف خربت ليس للمتولي أن يبيع الشجرة ويعمر الدار ولكن يكري الدار ويستعين بالكراء على عمارة الدار لا بالشجرة؛ كذا في الظهيرية
The fourteenth [issue]: In the Fatwas of Samarqand: [If] a tree is a waqf in a waqf house that has fallen into ruin, the administrator may not sell the tree and repair the house, but rather he rents out the house and uses the rent to assist in repairing the house, not [by selling] the tree; thus in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario: a waqf property includes a tree standing within a waqf house. The house becomes dilapidated and needs repair. The question is whether the custodian can sell the tree (which is part of the waqf corpus) to fund the repairs. The Hanafi fatwa from Samarqand states clearly that this is not permissible. The custodian cannot sell any part of the waqf's corpus (the tree) even for the purpose of repairing another part of the same waqf. Instead, he should rent out the house (as is) and use the rental income for repairs. This upholds the inviolability of the waqf corpus: it cannot be sold or alienated. Using rental income (which is a product of the waqf) is acceptable because it does not destroy the corpus.

Key Terms
شجرة وقف (shajarat waqf): A tree that is part of the waqf property, either planted on waqf land or included in the endowment.
يكري الدار (yukrī al-dār): To rent out the house (as a whole or in part) to generate income.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the custodian do to repair a ruined waqf house that contains a waqf tree?
A) Sell the tree to fund repairs.
B) Rent out the house and use the rent for repairs.
C) Request permission from the judge to sell the tree.
D) Abandon the house.

Key Takeaway
The waqf corpus is inviolable: no part may be sold, even for maintenance; use income generated from the waqf instead.

Ruling on Eating from Workers' Food During Waqf Construction
Determines permissibility for supervisors to eat workers' food.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissibility of eating from food provided for waqf construction workers and identify the conditions that affect the ruling.

Core Idea
Eating from workers' food is permissible only for those who actively encourage the work or when workers are few.

When a waqf property is under construction, food may be provided for the laborers. A natural question arises: can the supervisor (shādd) or engineer (muhandis) also eat from that food? The Hanafi school provides a conditional ruling based on the supervisor's role and the number of workers. This lesson examines the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating from the food provided for construction workers. The default ruling is mubah (permissible) only when certain conditions are met; otherwise, it becomes prohibited.
The ruling is not absolute – it depends on context.
2
Determine the first condition: encouragement of work
If the person (supervisor, engineer, or any individual) is present and actively encourages and urges the workers, then eating is permissible. This is because his presence contributes to the work's progress.
Encouragement must be real, not merely passive presence.
3
Determine the second condition: number of workers
If the person does not actively encourage the work, then the permissibility depends on the number of workers. If the workers are few, eating is permissible; if many, it is not, because taking food would reduce the workers' share.
'Few' is determined by custom and the overall sufficiency of food.
4
Apply the ruling to specific roles
The passage explicitly states that the overseer (shādd) and engineer (muhandis) are included in the ruling. Since they are integral to the project, they may eat with the workers under the same conditions.
This extends the ruling beyond ordinary workers to supervisors.
5
Understand the source and authority
The ruling is based on a case reported in al-Zahiriyya about a group collecting funds to build a bridge. It is considered a nawādir (rare transmission), but the conditional permission is the relied-upon (muftā bihi) position.
Later Hanafi works like al-Bahr al-Rā'iq adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة عشرة: هل يجوز الأكل من بنی خاناً الرملي : C قال كان قبله فإن كان يشتري من الغلة ما ذكرنا جاز له الشراء وإلا فلا .اهـ قوله : (وعليه الزيادة) قال في الأشباه : وهل يجوز للمتولي أن يشتري متاعاً بأكثر من قيمته ويبيعه ويصرفه على العمارة ويكون الربح على الوقف؟ الجواب : نعم كما حرره ابن وهبان اهـ. أقول: بينهما ما يشبه المخالفة إلا أن يقال : لما لم يلزم الأجل في مسألة القرض بقي مجرد شراء اليسير بثمن كثير فتمحض ضرراً على الوقف فلم تلزمه الزيادة فكانت على القيم بخلاف مسألة شراء المتاع وبيعه للزوم الأجل في جملة الثمن فتأمل اهـ. لكن قال المقدسي : إن ما في القنية يرد ما قاله ابن وهبان. قوله: (فسيلاً) طعام العملة . يوم العمارة؟ قالوا : إن حضر واللإرشاد والحث على العمل جاز الأكل وإلا فإن كانوا قليلاً جاز وإلا فلا ؛ ذكره في الظهيرية في قوم جمعوا الدراهم لعمارة القنطرة. وبهذا يعلم جواز أكل الشاد والمهندس معهم
The fifteenth [issue]: Is it permissible to eat from ... [garbled] ... the food of the workers on the day of construction? They said: If he is present and encourages and urges the work, eating is permissible; otherwise, if they are few, it is permissible, otherwise not. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyya regarding a group who collected dirhams for building a bridge. And by this it is known that it is permissible for the overseer (shadd) and the engineer (muhandis) to eat with them.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical question in waqf management: When food is provided for workers repairing a waqf construction (e.g., a bridge), may the supervisors or overseers also eat from it? The Hanafi ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the person (e.g., supervisor) is present to encourage and oversee the work, it is permissible for him to eat. (2) If he is not encouraging, then if the workers are few, it is permissible, but if many, it is not (because it would reduce the workers' share). This is based on a case reported in al-Zahiriyya of a group collecting funds for a bridge. The ruling is then extrapolated: the overseer (shadd) and engineer (muhandis) may also eat with the workers since they are engaged in the project. The intervening garbled text appears to be a different discussion about purchasing goods at inflated prices and may be a separate lesson, but it is embedded here.

Key Terms
شاد (shādd): The overseer or foreman of the construction project.
مهندس (muhandis): The engineer or architect supervising the construction.
عملة (ʿamalah): Workers or laborers involved in the construction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when may the overseer (shādd) eat from the workers' food during waqf construction?
A) Always, because he is supervising.
B) Only if the workers are few.
C) Only if he is present and encouraging the work.
D) Never, because it is for workers only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of supervisors eating from workers' food during waqf construction depends on active encouragement or, lacking that, a small workforce.

Conditions for Diverting Waqf Surplus to Another for the Same Mosque
Inter-madhhab (intra-Hanafi) dispute on mixing waqf revenues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions (unity of donor and unity of category) for diverting waqf surplus, and apply them to a real case.

Core Idea
Surplus from one mosque waqf may be diverted to another only if donor and purpose are identical; otherwise, the donor's conditions bind.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical waqf problem: when a mosque has multiple endowments, can the surplus from one be used for another? Two fatwa sources appear to conflict. The lesson dissects the conditions and shows how the later commentary harmonises them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
Ask: Under what circumstances can the surplus (fāḍil) from one waqf be spent on the purposes of another waqf when both are for the same mosque?
2
Analyse the first scenario from Fatāwā Khwārizm
If the donor (wāqif) is the same and the category (jihah) is the same — e.g., both waqfs are for the mosque but one for maintenance, one for the imam — the judge may divert surplus with local approval, because the donor's purpose is to revive the waqf.
Here, unity of donor AND unity of category are required.
3
Analyse the second scenario from al-Walwālijiyya
If the mosque has multiple waqfs with different donors, the custodian may mix all incomes and repair one waqf's property from another's surplus, because all belong to the mosque. Unity of mosque suffices.
This appears to allow mixing even if donor differs.
4
Reconcile the apparent conflict
The commentator reconciles: the permissive rule applies when all waqfs serve the same overarching purpose (the mosque). The restrictive rule applies when the categories (jihāt) are different (e.g., maintenance vs. personnel) — then donor unity is needed to protect specific conditions.
The later commentary in the next lesson may further clarify.
5
Apply to the Shaykhūniyya example
The passage concludes that the administrator of the Shaykhūniyya in Cairo cannot divert one waqf to another, likely because different donors or categories exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة عشرة : في البزازية : وقد تقرر في فتاوى خوارزم أن الواقف ومحل الوقف أعني الجهة إن اتحدت بأن كانا وقفاً على المسجد أحدهما إلى العمارة والآخر إلى إمامه أو مؤذنه والإمام والمؤذن لا يستقر لقلة المرسوم للحاكم الدين أن يصرف من فاضل وقف المصالح والعمارة إلى الإمام والمؤذن باستصواب أهل الصلاح من أهل المحلة إن كان الواقف متحداً لأن غرض الواقف إحياء وقفه وذلك يحصل بما قلنا، أما إذا اختلف الواقف أو اتحد الواقف واختلفت الجهة بأن بنى مدرسة ومسجداً وعين لكل وقفاً وفضل من غلة أحدهما لا يبدل شرط الواقف وكذا إذا اختلف الواقف لا الجهة يتبع شرط الواقف وقد علم بهذا التقرير إعمال الغلتين إحياء للوقف ورعاية شرط الواقف، هذا الحاصل من الفتاوى اهـ . وقد علم منه أنه لا يجوز لمتولي الشيخونية بالقاهرة صرف أحد الوقفين للآخر. وفي الولوالجية : مسجد له أوقاف مختلفة لا بأس للقيم أن يخلط غلتها كلها، وإن خرب حانوت منها فلا بأس بعمارته من غلة حانوت آخر لأن الكل للمسجد. هذا إذا كان الواقف واحداً، وإن كان الواقف مختلفاً فكذلك الجواب لأن المعنى يجمعهما اهـ.
The sixteenth [issue]: In al-Bazzaziyya: It is established in the Fatwas of Khwarizm that if the waqf donor and the place of the waqf, meaning the category (jihah), are the same—such as both being a waqf for the mosque, one for maintenance and the other for its imam or muezzin, and the imam and muezzin are not settled due to the smallness of the stipend—then the religious judge (al-hakim al-din) may spend from the surplus of the waqf of benefits and maintenance to the imam and muezzin with the approval of the righteous people of the neighborhood, if the donor is the same, because the donor's purpose is to revive his waqf, and that is achieved by what we said. However, if the donor differs, or the donor is the same but the category (jihah) differs—such as building a school and a mosque, and designating a waqf for each, and there is a surplus from one of them—the condition of the donor is not to be changed. Similarly, if the donor differs but not the category, the condition of the donor is followed. And by this explanation it is understood that the two incomes are used to revive the waqf and observe the donor's condition. This is the gist of the fatwas. And from this it is known that it is not permissible for the administrator of the Shaykhuniyya in Cairo to divert one waqf to the other. And in al-Walwaljiyya: A mosque has different waqfs; there is no harm for the custodian to mix all their incomes, and if a shop among them collapses, there is no harm in repairing it from the income of another shop because all belong to the mosque. This is if the donor is one; and if the donor is different, the answer is the same because the meaning unites them.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is a complex Hanafi ruling on whether the surplus from one waqf can be used for the purpose of another waqf when both are for the same mosque. There are two scenarios based on the identity of the donor (waqif) and the category (jihah, i.e., the specific purpose like maintenance or imam stipend). The Fatwas of Khwarizm state: If the donor is the same and the category is the same (e.g., both are for the mosque, one for maintenance, one for personnel), then if one surplus exists, the judge can redirect it with community approval. But if the donor or category differs (e.g., school vs. mosque), the donor's conditions must be strictly followed. The passage then cites al-Walwaljiyya, which appears to contradict by allowing mixing of all waqfs for the same mosque regardless of donor, because all ultimately serve the mosque. This is resolved by the later commentary in the next lesson. The practical conclusion is that for the Shaykhuniyya in Cairo (a specific institution), one waqf cannot be spent on another.

Key Terms
جهة (jihah): The specific purpose or category of the waqf (e.g., maintenance, imam, muezzin).
فاضل وقف (fāḍil waqf): The surplus income from a waqf after fulfilling its designated purpose.
واقف (wāqif): The donor who establishes the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled Hanafi position in this lesson, when can the surplus from a mosque waqf for 'maintenance' be used for the imam's stipend?
A) Only if the donor of both waqfs is the same.
B) Only if the imam's stipend waqf has a deficit.
C) Only if the judge and community approve, regardless of donor.
D) Only if both waqfs have the same donor and the category is the same (both are for the mosque's general benefit).

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of diverting waqf surplus hinges on whether the donors and categories (jihāt) are the same; if categories differ, donor unity is required; otherwise, mixing is allowed for the same mosque.

Priority in Rebuilding a Ruined Ribat
Ruling on priority after complete rebuilding of a waqf inn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on priority rights when a ruined ribat is rebuilt and apply it to cases of identical versus altered reconstruction.

Core Idea
Priority in a rebuilt ribat depends on whether the new building is identical to the old: no priority if identical, priority if size changed.

This short but important ruling from al-Bazzaziyya clarifies the rights of original residents in a waqf inn after it collapses and is rebuilt. The key distinction is whether the rebuild is an exact replica or involves an increase or decrease in size.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible outcomes of the rebuild
The passage specifies two scenarios: (1) the new building is reconstructed identically in every aspect ('from scratch' and 'without changing its layout'), and (2) the new building is increased or decreased in size relative to the original.
The term 'from every angle' (من كل وجه) emphasizes a complete replica.
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
In the first scenario (identical rebuild), the original residents are not given priority over new applicants—all are equal. In the second scenario (size altered), the original residents are given priority.
The ruling uses 'لا يكون الأولون أولى' for identical, and 'فالأولون أولى' for altered.
3
Understand the rationale behind the distinction
The difference in ruling likely stems from the principle that a complete rebuild severs the continuity of the original waqf, making the new building a fresh endowment. An alteration (increase or decrease) retains a connection to the original, thus preserving the prior rights of beneficiaries.
This rationale aligns with broader waqf rules on changes to endowed property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة عشرة : في البزازية : وإذا انهدم رباط المختلفة وبنى بناء جديداً من كل وجه لا يكون الأولون أولى من غيرهم وإن لم يغير ترتيبه الأول إلا أنه إن زيد أو نقص فالأولون أولى اهـ.
The seventeenth [issue]: In al-Bazzaziyya: If a ribat (waqf inn) of various [residents] collapses and he builds a new building completely from scratch, the first [residents] are not given priority over others, even if he did not change its original layout. However, if it is increased or decreased [in size], then the first ones are given priority.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This ruling deals with a waqf ribat (a hospice or inn for travelers or the poor) that collapses and is rebuilt. The question is whether the original residents (the ones living there before the collapse) have priority to occupy the new building. The Hanafi ruling from al-Bazzaziyya distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the ribat is rebuilt identically (same layout, same number of rooms), the original residents do not have priority over new applicants; all are equal. (2) If the new building is larger or smaller than the original, then the original residents do have priority. The rationale may be that a complete rebuild changes the nature of the waqf, whereas a modification (increase or decrease) retains continuity with the original, thus preserving their right.

Key Terms
رباط (ribāṭ): A waqf inn or hospice providing lodging, often for travelers, the poor, or Sufis.
الأولون (al-awwalūn): The original residents or beneficiaries who occupied the ribat before its collapse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The original residents.
B) New applicants.
C) No one has priority; they are equal.
D) The original residents have priority only if they contributed to the rebuild.

Key Takeaway
The priority of original residents in a rebuilt ribat depends on whether the new building is identical (no priority) or altered in size (priority).

Building on Waqf Land: The Custodian's Building and Ownership
Distinguishes building on waqf land by custodian vs. stranger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a building erected by the waqf custodian on waqf land, and distinguish when it becomes waqf vs. remains the custodian's property.

Core Idea
A custodian's building on waqf land becomes waqf unless he explicitly declares it for himself.

The status of structures built on waqf land is a critical issue in waqf jurisprudence. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq distinguishes between a custodian (mutawalli) and a stranger (ajnabi), and introduces the key role of declaration. The ruling protects the waqf while allowing the custodian to claim personal ownership if he openly declares his intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The passage mentions two persons: the mutawalli (custodian) and the ajnabi (stranger). Their treatment differs.
2
Analyze the mutawalli's three scenarios
The mutawalli builds (1) with waqf funds, (2) with his own money intending waqf, or (3) without mentioning intent. In all three, the building becomes waqf.
The default is that the building becomes part of the waqf.
3
Examine the exception
If the mutawalli explicitly attests that he built it for himself, then it remains his property.
The declaration must be witnessed.
4
Contrast with the stranger
For the stranger, the ruling is different—implied that his building does not automatically become waqf.
The passage does not elaborate on the stranger's case, but the contrast is clear.
5
Extract the legal principle
The ruling emphasizes the mutawalli's authority and the importance of declaration. Without declaration, the building is annexed to the waqf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامنة عشرة : بنى المتولي في عرصة الوقف من مال الوقف أو من ماله للوقف أو لم يذكر شيئاً كان وقفاً بخلاف الأجنبي، وإن أشهد أنه بناه لنفسه كان ملكاً له وإن متولياً؛ كذا في البزازية
The eighteenth [issue]: If the administrator (mutawalli) builds in the courtyard of the waqf from the funds of the waqf, or from his own money for the waqf, or does not mention anything, it becomes waqf, unlike a stranger. And if he attests that he built it for himself, it is his property even if he is the administrator; thus in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This ruling clarifies the legal status of structures built on waqf land. There are two parties: the administrator (mutawalli) and an outsider (ajnabi). (1) If the mutawalli builds on waqf land using waqf funds, his own money with the intent for the waqf, or without specifying, the building becomes part of the waqf (it is added to the endowment). (2) If the mutawalli explicitly states and witnesses that he built it for himself (personal ownership), then it remains his property, even though he is the administrator. (3) For an outsider (ajnabi), the ruling is different (implied: an outsider's building on waqf land without permission would not automatically become waqf). This protects the waqf from unauthorized appropriation while recognizing the possibility of personal investment by the administrator if clearly stated.

Key Terms
عرصة الوقف (ʿarṣat al-waqf): The open land or courtyard belonging to the waqf.
أجنبي (ajnabī): A person who is not the custodian or administrator of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It becomes his personal property.
B) It becomes part of the waqf.
C) It must be removed.
D) It is shared between him and the waqf.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is the identity of the builder and, for the custodian, the explicit declaration of personal intent.

Reconciliation of Contradictory Fatwas on Mixing Waqf Revenues
Harmonizes two fatwa sources on waqf revenue mixing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how al-Ramli reconciles the apparent contradiction between two Hanafi fatwas regarding the mixing of waqf revenues and apply the principle of unification of category (jihah).

Core Idea
Fatwa contradictions dissolve when we identify the category (jihah) as the unifying principle.

When legal authorities appear to contradict each other, a skilled faqih must look deeper. In this passage, the Hanafi scholar al-Ramli harmonizes two seemingly opposing fatwas from al-Walwaljiyya and al-Bazzaziyya on the permissibility of mixing waqf revenues. He shows that the apparent conflict disappears once we understand that one ruling applies when the category (jihah) is unified, and the other when it is not. This lesson will guide you through his method of tawfiq (reconciliation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting fatwas
Locate the rulings from al-Walwaljiyya and al-Bazzaziyya as presented in the text. Note the apparent contradiction: al-Walwaljiyya permits mixing revenues for the same mosque regardless of donor; al-Bazzaziyya elsewhere restricts mixing when the category (jihah) or donor differs.
The text quotes al-Bazzaziyya allowing mixing for a mosque, which actually agrees with al-Walwaljiyya.
2
Examine al-Ramli's reconciliation method
Al-Ramli argues that the conflict is only apparent. He points out that al-Walwaljiyya's ruling applies when the category (jihah) is unified and the donors' conditions are compatible. Al-Bazzaziyya's earlier prohibition refers to cases where the category differs, not to the unified case.
Reconciliation (tawfiq) does not discard either source but identifies the different contexts.
3
Apply the principle of jihah
The reconciliation hinges on jihah (category/purpose). If the waqf revenues are for the same mosque (unified jihah), mixing is permissible. If the jihah is different (e.g., one for the mosque, another for a school), the donors' conditions must be followed strictly.
The unity of jihah overrides differences in donors.
4
Evaluate the practical outcome
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that mixing is allowed for a single mosque when the category is unified, even if donors differ. This resolves the conflict without weakening either fatwa source.
The custodian (qayyim) may combine revenues for repairs and maintenance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الرملي : لا مخالفة ما في الولوالجية والبزازية لأن ما في الولوالجية ضد اتحاد الجهة وتوافق الشرطين من الواقفين تأمل. وفي البزازية في الرابع في المسجد وما يتصل به مسجد له أوقاف مختلفة لا بأس للقيم أن يخلط غلتها، وإن خرب حانوت فيها لا بأس بعمارته من غلة حانوت آخر اتحد الواقف أولا اهـ. فهو كما تراه عين ما في الولوالجية .اهـ. وانظر هذا التوفيق مع قول البزازية الذي قدمه المؤلف، وكذا إذا اختلف الواقف لا الجهة يتبع شرط الواقف قوله : (بخلاف الأجنبي قال في الأشباه : وإن لم يكن متولياً فإنه بإذن المتولي ليرجع فهو وقف وإلا فإن بنى للوقف فوقف، وإن لنفسه أو أطلق رفعه لو لم
Al-Ramli said: There is no contradiction between what is in al-Walwaljiyya and al-Bazzaziyya, because what is in al-Walwaljiyya is against the unity of category (jihah) and the agreement of the conditions from the donors. Reflect. And in al-Bazzaziyya, in the fourth [section] on the mosque and what pertains to it: A mosque has different endowments; there is no harm for the custodian to mix all their incomes, and if a shop among them collapses, there is no harm in repairing it from the income of another shop, whether the donor is one or not. See, it is exactly what is in al-Walwaljiyya. And consider this reconciliation with the statement of al-Bazzaziyya that the author presented earlier: 'And likewise if the donor differs but not the category, the condition of the donor is followed.' His saying: '(Unlike the stranger).' He said in al-Ashbah: If he is not the administrator, then with the permission of the administrator to return, it is waqf; otherwise, if he builds for the waqf, it is waqf; and if for himself or absolutely, it is raised if not...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator al-Ramli, who attempts to resolve an apparent contradiction between two earlier sources: al-Bazzaziyya (which in one place forbids mixing waqf revenues if donor or category differ) and al-Walwaljiyya (which permits mixing all revenues for the same mosque regardless of donor). Al-Ramli argues that there is no real contradiction. He points out that al-Walwaljiyya's ruling applies when the category (jihah) is unified and the conditions of the donors are compatible, whereas al-Bazzaziyya's earlier statement addresses cases where category differs. He also cites a passage from al-Bazzaziyya itself that allows mixing for a mosque, which actually agrees with al-Walwaljiyya. The reconciliation shows that mixing is permissible as long as the overall purpose serves the same mosque and the donors' conditions are not violated. The text ends with a comment on building by a stranger, quoting al-Ashbah, but the OCR cuts off.

Key Terms
توفيق (tawfīq): Reconciliation or harmonization between seemingly conflicting legal rulings.
جهة (jihah): Category, purpose, or direction of a waqf. Here, it refers to the unified purpose (e.g., serving the same mosque) that permits mixing revenues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does al-Ramli reconcile the permission in al-Walwaljiyya to mix waqf revenues with the restriction in al-Bazzaziyya?
A) He declares al-Walwaljiyya invalid.
B) He says they apply to different situations (unified vs. different category).
C) He says mixing is always prohibited.
D) He says the donor's condition is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa contradictions can often be resolved by identifying the governing principle (jihah) and applying it consistently, preserving the authority of all sources.

Eating from Waqf Construction Funds
Ruling on permissibility of workers eating from collected funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which workers may eat from waqf construction funds and apply the ruling to scenarios involving overseers and engineers.

Core Idea
Food from waqf funds is permissible only when the collector encourages work or the workers are few.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq addresses a practical fiqh question: may workers and supervisors eat from funds collected for a charitable construction project? The answer depends on contextual factors such as the presence of the fund collector and the number of workers. Understanding these conditions prevents misuse of waqf assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its categories
The act is eating from collected funds for a bridge. The passage distinguishes three scenarios: collector present for guidance, workers few, or workers many.
The ruling is conditional.
2
Understand the condition for permissibility
If the collector is present and actively guiding/encouraging work, implicit consent exists, so eating is allowed. If not, only a small number of workers may eat; otherwise it is not permitted.
'Few' is relative but indicates negligible consumption.
3
Extend the ruling to supervisors and engineers
The passage explicitly includes the overseer (shādd) and engineer (muhandis) in the same permissibility, as they are also involved in the work.
They are not workers but are included.
4
Note the source and authority
The ruling is from al-Ẓāhiriyyah, a Hanafi source, and applies to waqf funds. It is an exception to the general inviolability of waqf property.
This is a specific ruling within waqf law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طعام العملة. يوم العمارة؟ قالوا : إن حضر واللإرشاد والحث على العمل جاز الأكل وإلا فإن كانوا قليلاً جاز وإلا فلا ؛ ذكره في الظهيرية في قوم جمعوا الدراهم لعمارة القنطرة. وبهذا يعلم جواز أكل الشاد والمهندس معهم
The food of the workers. On the day of construction? They said: If [the one who collects] is present for guidance and encouragement to work, eating is permissible. Otherwise, if they are few, it is permissible; otherwise no. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyyah concerning a people who collected dirhams for the construction of a bridge. By this it is known that it is permissible for the overseer and the engineer to eat with them.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of workers and supervisors eating from funds collected for a charitable construction project (here a bridge). The ruling distinguishes between cases: if the person responsible for the funds is present and encourages work (perhaps indicating implicit consent), then eating is allowed. If not, then only if the workers are few (so the amount is negligible) is it allowed; otherwise it is not allowed because it would be a diversion of waqf funds. The source is al-Zahiriyyah. The ruling extends to the overseer (shadd) and engineer (muhandis) as they are also involved in the work.

Key Terms
العملة (al-ʿamalah): The workers hired for construction
الشاد (al-shādd): The overseer or supervisor of the work
المهندس (al-muhandis): The engineer or architect

C) Only if the collector is absent and the workers are many

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of eating from waqf construction funds depends on the presence of the collector or the small number of workers.

Transferring Surplus Between Different Waqf Funds
Ruling on transferring waqf surplus based on founder and beneficiary identity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for transferring surplus between waqfs and apply the condition that the founder's intention must be preserved.

Core Idea
Waqf surplus can only be diverted when the beneficiary is the same, or when all waqfs serve the same purpose (e.g., a mosque).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical problem: what happens when one waqf fund has surplus while another is deficient? The Hanafi school provides nuanced rules based on the identity of the founder and the beneficiary. Understanding these rules is crucial for trustees and judges managing awqaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key variables
The ruling depends on two variables: whether the waqif (founder) is the same or different, and whether the jihah (beneficiary/purpose) is the same or different.
These variables create three distinct scenarios.
2
Extract rulings for each scenario
From Fatawa Khwarazm: if both waqif and jihah are the same, transfer is permitted with judicial approval. If waqif is same but jihah differs, transfer is not allowed. If waqif differs but jihah is the same, transfer is allowed (per al-Walwalijiyyah for a mosque).
The text also mentions an exception for a single mosque with multiple waqfs.
3
Note the exception for a single mosque
Al-Walwalijiyyah states that for a mosque with multiple waqfs (even from different founders), mixing yields is allowed because all are for the mosque.
This overrides the general rule when the beneficiary (jihah) is physically the same entity.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
The permissibility is based on istihsan: the founder's purpose is to revive the waqf and ensure its continuity. Transferring surplus achieves this purpose without violating the founder's condition if the beneficiary is unified.
The proof is aqli (rational): 'li-anna gharda al-wāqifi iḥyā'u waqfihi'.
5
Apply to a counterexample
The text cites the Shaykhuniyyah in Cairo: its two waqfs cannot be mixed because they have different beneficiaries. This illustrates when transfer is prohibited.
Always check the conditions of each waqf before any transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة عشرة : في البزازية : وقد تقرر في فتاوى خوارزم أن الواقف ومحل الوقف أعني الجهة إن اتحدت بأن كانا وقفاً على المسجد أحدهما إلى العمارة والآخر إلى إمامه أو مؤذنه والإمام والمؤذن لا يستقر لقلة المرسوم للحاكم الدين أن يصرف من فاضل وقف المصالح والعمارة إلى الإمام والمؤذن باستصواب أهل الصلاح من أهل المحلة إن كان الواقف متحداً لأن غرض الواقف إحياء وقفه وذلك يحصل بما قلنا، أما إذا اختلف الواقف أو اتحد الواقف واختلفت الجهة بأن بنى مدرسة ومسجداً وعين لكل وقفاً وفضل من غلة أحدهما لا يبدل شرط الواقف وكذا إذا اختلف الواقف لا الجهة يتبع شرط الواقف وقد علم بهذا التقرير إعمال الغلتين إحياء للوقف ورعاية شرط الواقف، هذا الحاصل من الفتاوى اهـ . وقد علم منه أنه لا يجوز لمتولي الشيخونية بالقاهرة صرف أحد الوقفين للآخر. وفي الولوالجية : مسجد له أوقاف مختلفة لا بأس للقيم أن يخلط غلتها كلها، وإن خرب حانوت منها فلا بأس بعمارته من غلة حانوت آخر لأن الكل للمسجد. هذا إذا كان الواقف واحداً، وإن كان الواقف مختلفاً فكذلك الجواب لأن المعنى يجمعهما اهـ.
The sixteenth [issue]: In al-Bazzaziyyah: It has been established in the fatawa of Khwarazm that if the founder and the place of the waqf, meaning the beneficiary, are unified, such that both are a waqf upon the mosque, one for construction and the other for its imam or mu'adhdhin, and the imam and mu'adhdhin do not have a stable income due to the smallness of the stipend, then it is permissible for the religious judge to spend from the surplus of the waqf of the welfare and construction to the imam and mu'adhdhin with the approval of the righteous people of the neighborhood, if the founder is one, because the purpose of the founder is to revive his waqf, and that is achieved by what we said. As for when the founder differs or the founder is one but the beneficiary differs, such as building a school and a mosque and designating a waqf for each, and there is a surplus from the yield of one, then the condition of the founder is not to be changed. Similarly, if the founder differs but the beneficiary does not, the condition of the founder is followed. By this exposition it is known that both yields are to be used for the revival of the waqf and observance of the founder's condition. This is the conclusion from the fatawa. From this it is known that it is not permissible for the trustee of the Shaykhuniyyah in Cairo to spend one of the two waqfs for the other. And in al-Walwalijiyyah: A mosque has various waqfs; there is no harm for the caretaker to mix all their yields, and if a shop among them is ruined, there is no harm in repairing it from the yield of another shop because all is for the mosque. This is if the founder is one. If the founder is different, the answer is likewise because the meaning unites them.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when surplus from one waqf can be diverted to another. Two sources are cited: Fatawa Khwarazm and al-Walwalijiyyah. The key factors are the identity of the founder (waqif) and the beneficiary (jihah). If both are the same (e.g., both waqfs are for the same mosque), then surplus can be transferred from the construction fund to the imam's stipend if needed, with judicial approval. If the founder is one but beneficiaries differ (e.g., school vs. mosque), or founders differ, the original conditions of each waqf must be followed. An exception is given in al-Walwalijiyyah: for a mosque with multiple waqfs, mixing yields is allowed regardless of whether the founder is one or multiple, because all are for the same mosque. The ruling also states that the trustee of Sheikhuniyyah in Cairo may not divert funds between its two waqfs, likely because they have different beneficiaries.

Key Terms
الواقف (al-wāqif): The person who establishes the waqf (founder)
الجهة (al-jihah): The beneficiary or purpose of the waqf
الشرط (al-shart): The condition stipulated by the founder
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that gives priority to a stronger, more appropriate ruling over a strict analogy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition does al-Walwalijiyyah permit mixing the yields of different waqfs?
A) Only if the founders are the same
B) Only if the beneficiaries are different
C) If all waqfs are for the same mosque, even if founders differ
D) Only if the judge approves

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits transferring waqf surplus only when the beneficiary is unified or when all waqfs serve the same purpose, preserving the founder's intent through istihsan.

Trustee Building on Waqf Land
Ruling on trustee building on waqf land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a trustee builds on waqf land and identify the condition that makes the building the trustee's personal property.

Core Idea
A trustee's building on waqf land becomes waqf unless he explicitly declares it as his own.

This short ruling from al-Bazzaziyyah clarifies a common issue in waqf administration. When a trustee constructs a building on waqf land, the default ruling is that the building becomes part of the waqf. However, the trustee can retain ownership by making a clear declaration. The rule differs for a stranger, whose building does not automatically become waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor
Determine who is building on the waqf land: a trustee (mutawallī) or a stranger (ajnabī). The ruling differs based on this.
A trustee has authority over the waqf; a stranger does not.
2
Examine the source of funds and intention
If the trustee uses waqf funds or his own money with the intention of benefiting the waqf, or if he does not state any intention, the building becomes waqf.
The text says 'or does not mention anything' – silence implies intention for the waqf.
3
Check for explicit declaration
If the trustee makes a formal declaration (with witnesses) that he built it for himself, the building remains his personal property even though he is the trustee.
This is the exception: explicit declaration overrides the default.
4
Contrast with a stranger
A stranger's building on waqf land does not automatically become waqf; it remains the stranger's property unless he intends otherwise with permission.
The default for a stranger is the opposite of the trustee's default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامنة عشرة : بنى المتولي في عرصة الوقف من مال الوقف أو من ماله للوقف أو لم يذكر شيئاً كان وقفاً بخلاف الأجنبي، وإن أشهد أنه بناه لنفسه كان ملكاً له وإن متولياً؛ كذا في البزازية
The eighteenth [issue]: If the trustee builds on the waqf land from waqf funds or from his own money for the waqf, or does not mention anything, it becomes waqf, unlike a stranger. And if he makes witnesses that he built it for himself, it becomes his property even if he is a trustee; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between a trustee (mutawalli) and a stranger (ajnabi) when building on waqf land. If the trustee builds using waqf funds or his own money with the intention of adding to the waqf, or if he does not specify his intention, the building becomes part of the waqf. However, if he explicitly declares (with witnesses) that he built it for himself, it remains his personal property, despite being a trustee. A stranger's building on waqf land is not automatically waqf; he would need permission or explicit intention. This is from al-Bazzaziyyah.

Key Terms
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The trustee or administrator of the waqf
عرصة الوقف (ʿarṣat al-waqf): The land or courtyard of the waqf
الأجنبي (al-ajnabī): A stranger, someone not a trustee or beneficiary of the waqf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a trustee do for his building on waqf land to be considered his personal property?
A) Use his own money
B) Build with the intention of benefiting the waqf
C) Make a formal declaration with witnesses that it is for himself
D) Obtain permission from the beneficiaries

Key Takeaway
A trustee's building on waqf land becomes waqf by default, but a clear witnessed declaration to the contrary makes it his personal property.

Caretaker Not Entitled to Wages for Construction Work
Ruling on caretaker's wages for physical work on waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding a waqf caretaker performing physical labor and explain why he cannot receive additional wages.

Core Idea
A waqf caretaker cannot combine supervisory salary with labor wages; doing the work himself is part of his duty.

This passage addresses a common scenario where a waqf caretaker personally undertakes construction or maintenance. The ruling clarifies that he is not entitled to extra wages for that labor, as his existing supervision salary covers those duties. This prevents double compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the caretaker doing? He works in construction like a hired laborer. The ruling: he is not entitled to a wage for that work.
The act is working as a laborer on waqf property.
2
Identify the parties and roles
The person is the qayyim (caretaker) who already receives a salary for supervision. He performs physical labor himself.
He has two roles: caretaker and worker. The ruling addresses the conflict.
3
Understand the legal reason ('illa)
The wage of supervision (ujrat al-qawama) and the wage of labor (ujrat al-‘amal) cannot be combined for one person. The supervision salary already encompasses the duty of overseeing construction, so doing the work himself does not create a separate entitlement.
The combination is prevented because the duties overlap.
4
Note the source and authority
The ruling is cited from al-Qunyah, a later Hanafi text. It is a standard position in the madhhab.
The author also mentions it will come later, indicating its importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسعة عشرة : إذا عمل القيم في عمارة المسجد والوقف كعمل الأجير لا يستحق أجراً لأنه لا يجتمع له أجر القوامة وأجر العمل؛ كذا في القنية وسيأتي أيضاً
The nineteenth [issue]: When the caretaker works in the construction of the mosque and the waqf like the work of a hired laborer, he is not entitled to a wage because the wage of supervision and the wage of work cannot be combined for him; thus in al-Qunyah, and it will also come later.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage rules that a waqf caretaker (qayyim) who personally performs construction or maintenance work cannot claim an additional wage for that labor. His existing salary as caretaker (ujrat al-qawama) covers his duties, and he cannot receive a separate wage as a laborer (ajir). This is because the two roles conflict: he is already compensated for overseeing the waqf, so doing the work himself is part of his duty, not extra work. The source is al-Qunyah.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The caretaker or supervisor of the waqf property
أجر القوامة (ujrat al-qawāmah): Salary for supervision and management
أجر العمل (ujrat al-ʿamal): Wage for physical labor

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He receives both his caretaker salary and labor wages
B) He receives only his caretaker salary, not extra labor wages
C) He receives only labor wages, not his caretaker salary
D) He receives nothing because he is acting outside his duties

Key Takeaway
A waqf caretaker cannot receive additional wages for personally performing construction or maintenance work because his supervision salary already covers such duties.

Using Waqf Funds for Non-Mosque Property to Protect the Mosque
Ruling on using mosque funds to cover a market roof to protect mosque from sun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a mosque caretaker may spend waqf funds on non-mosque property and apply it to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Mosque funds may be used for external repairs if necessary to protect the mosque from harm.

This lesson presents a narrow exception to the general rule that waqf funds are restricted to the waqf property. The text from al-Qunyah, cited in Bahr al-Ra'iq, permits a caretaker to spend mosque money on a market roof when the exposed roof causes excessive heat in the neighboring summer mosque. The permission is limited to the amount needed to repel the harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize that an uncovered market roof is causing harmful heat to enter the summer mosque due to direct sunlight.
The harm must be actual and significant.
2
State the ruling
The caretaker (qayyim) is permitted to cover the market roof using mosque waqf funds.
This is an exception to the usual restriction on waqf funds.
3
Determine the limitation
The expenditure must be limited to the extent necessary to repel the harm — no more.
Excessive spending is not allowed; only what is needed to protect the mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العشرون : لو انكشف سقف السوق فغلب الحر على المسجد الصيفي لوقوع الشمس فيه فللقيم ستر سقف السوق من مال المسجد بقدر ما يندفع به هذا القدر ؛ كذا في القنية
The twentieth [issue]: If the roof of the market is uncovered and the heat overwhelms the summer mosque due to the sun falling into it, then the caretaker may cover the roof of the market from the mosque funds to the extent that this amount of [harm] is repelled; thus in al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This ruling addresses a situation where the mosque suffers from excessive heat because an adjacent market's roof is damaged, allowing sunlight to enter the mosque. The caretaker (qayyim) is permitted to spend from the mosque's waqf funds to repair or cover the market roof, but only to the extent necessary to protect the mosque. This is because the mosque's benefit justifies spending on non-mosque property if it indirectly protects the mosque. The source is al-Qunyah.

Key Terms
المسجد الصيفي (al-masjid al-ṣayfī): The summer mosque, i.e., an open area used for prayer in summer
القيم (al-qayyim): The caretaker of the waqf (mosque)

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Never, because mosque funds are exclusively for the mosque building
D) Only if the market owner agrees to repay

Key Takeaway
Mosque waqf funds may be exceptionally used for external repairs if the harm to the mosque is direct and the expense is limited to repelling it.
