تجوز إجارته وهذا في الدور والحوانيت وأما الأراضي؛ فإن كان الواقف شرط تقديم العشر والخراج وسائر المؤن فليس للموقوف عليه أن يؤاجر، وإن لم يشترط ذلك يجب أن يجوز ويكون الخراج والمؤنة عليه والدعوى من الموقوف عليه غير مسموعة على الصحيح وبه يفتى؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين فإن قلت: إذا لم يصح إيجاره ما حكم الأجرة إذا آجرها؟ قلت: أن تكون للوقف ولم أره صريحاً. ولو قالوا عمرها المتولي أو القاضي لكان أولى فظاهر قولهم إنما يملك الإجارة المتولي أو القاضي أن للقاضي الاستقلال بالإجارة ولو أبى المتولي إلا أن يكون المراد التوزيع فالقاضي يؤجرها إن لم يكن لها متول أو كان لها وأبى الأصلح، وأما مع حضور المتولي فليس للقاضي ذلك وستزداد وضوحاً إن شاء الله تعالى بعد. ولم يذكر الشارحون حكم العمارة من المتولي أو القاضي هل هي مملوكة لمن له السكني أو لا؟ وفي المحيط : فإن أجر القيم وأنفق الأجرة في العمارة فتلك العمارة المحدثة تكون لصاحب السكني لأن الأجرة بدل المنفعة وملك المنفعة كانت مستحقة لصاحب السكني فكذا بدل المنفعة تكون له والقيم إنما أجر لأجله .اهـ. ومقتضاه أنه لو مات تكون ميراثاً كما لو عمرها بنفسه. وفي فتح القدير : ولو لم يرض الموقوف عليه السكني بالعمارة ولم يجد من يستأجرها لم أر حكم هذه في المنقول من المذهب، والحال فيها يؤدي إلى أن تصير نقضاً على الأرض كوماً تسفوه الرياح، وخطر لي أن يخيره القاضي بين يعمرها ليستوفي منفعتها وبين أن يردها إلى ورثة الواقف .اهـ. وهو عجيب لأنهم صرحوا باستبدال الوقف إذا خرب وصار لا ينتفع به وه شامل للأرض والدار قال في الذخيرة وفي المنتقى قال هشام: سمعت محمداً يقول : الوقف إذا صار بحيث لا ينتفع به المساكين فللقاضي أن يبيعه ويشتري بثمنه غيره وليس ذلك إلا للقاضي .اهـ. وأما عود الوقف بعد خرابه إلى ملك الواقف أو ورثته فقد قدمنا ضعفه والحاصل أن الموقوف عليه السكنى إذا امتنع من العمارة ولم يوجد مستأجر باعها القاضي واشترى بثمنها ما يكون وقفاً، وفي الولوالجية خان أو رباط سبيل أراد أن يخرب يؤاجره المتولي وينفق عليه فإذا صار معموراً لا يؤاجره لأنه لو لم يؤاجره يندرس اهـ . لكن ظاهر كلام المشايخ أن محل الاستبدال عند التعذر إنما هو الأرض لا البيت وقد حققناه في رسالة في الاستبدال قوله : ويصرف نقضه إلى عمارته إن احتاج وإلا حفظه للاحتياج ولا يقسمه بين مستحقي الوقف ...
It is permissible to lease it, and this applies to houses and shops. As for lands: if the waqif stipulated the payment of the tithe, land tax, and all expenses, then the beneficiary may not lease. If he did not stipulate that, it must be permissible, and the land tax and expenses are upon him, and the claim of the beneficiary is not heard according to the correct view, and with it fatwa is given; thus in Jami' al-Fusulayn. If you say: if his leasing is not valid, what is the ruling of the rent if he leased? I say: it belongs to the waqf, and I have not seen it explicitly. If they said: the mutawalli or the qadi built it, it would be better. So the apparent meaning of their statement that only the mutawalli or the qadi have the power of leasing is that the qadi has independence in leasing even if the mutawalli refuses, unless the intended meaning is distribution. So the qadi leases it if there is no mutawalli for it, or if there is one but he refuses what is more beneficial. As for when the mutawalli is present, the qadi does not have that, and it will become clearer later, God willing. The commentators did not mention the ruling on building by the mutawalli or the qadi: whether it is owned by the one entitled to residence or not. In al-Muhit: if the administrator leased and spent the rent on building, then that new building belongs to the owner of the residence because the rent is the substitute for the usufruct, and ownership of the usufruct was due to the owner of the residence, so also the substitute for the usufruct belongs to him, and the administrator only leased for his sake. Its import is that if he dies, it is inherited as if he had built it himself. In Fath al-Qadir: if the beneficiary of the residence does not consent to the building and finds no one to rent it, I have not seen the ruling on this in the transmitted [texts] of the madhhab, and the situation leads to it becoming rubble on the ground, a mound that winds blow away. It occurred to me that the qadi gives him a choice between building it to receive its benefit or returning it to the heirs of the waqif. This is strange because they explicitly allowed substitution (istibdal) of the waqf when it becomes ruined and unusable, and this includes land and house. It is said in al-Dhakhira and al-Muntaqa: Hisham said: I heard Muhammad say: when the waqf becomes such that the poor cannot benefit from it, the qadi may sell it and buy another with its price, and that is only for the qadi. As for the return of the waqf after its ruin to the ownership of the waqif or his heirs, we have already stated its weakness. The conclusion is that if the beneficiary of the residence refuses to build and no tenant is found, the qadi sells it and buys with its price what becomes a waqf. In al-Walwaljiyya: a khan or a way-side inn that is about to fall into ruin: the mutawalli leases it and spends on it, and when it becomes habitable, he does not lease it because if he does not lease it, it will become obliterated. But the apparent speech of the shuyukh is that the place of substitution when there is difficulty is only land, not the house, and we have verified this in a treatise on substitution. He said: and he spends its demolished materials on its building if needed, otherwise he keeps it for need, and does not distribute it among the beneficiaries of the waqf.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It covers the permissibility of leasing waqf property (houses and shops) and the conditions for land. If the waqif stipulated payment of taxes and expenses, the beneficiary cannot lease; if not, leasing is allowed and the expenses are on the beneficiary. The claim of the beneficiary about inability to lease is not heard. The rent, if leased improperly, belongs to the waqf. The text then discusses authority: the mutawalli or qadi can lease. The qadi can lease if there is no mutawalli or if the mutawalli refuses what is beneficial. But if the mutawalli is present, the qadi cannot lease. The building by the mutawalli using rent money belongs to the beneficiary of the residence, and if he dies it is inherited. If the beneficiary refuses to build and no tenant is found, the qadi may sell the property and buy another waqf. The text notes a difference of opinion about substitution (istibdal): some limit it to land, but the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq wrote a treatise allowing it for both. The passage concludes with the ruling on demolished materials (naqd) which are to be used for repair or kept for future need, not distributed.

Key Terms
الموقوف عليه (al-mawquf 'alayhi): The beneficiary of the waqf, i.e., the one entitled to its usufruct or rent.
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The person appointed by the waqif or by a judge to manage the waqf property.
القاضي (al-qadi): The judge with general supervisory authority over waqf properties, especially when there is no mutawalli or when the mutawalli fails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible for the beneficiary of a waqf land to lease it according to this passage?
A) Always, because the beneficiary owns the land.
B) Only if the waqif did not stipulate payment of taxes and expenses.
C) Only with the permission of the qadi.
D) It is never permissible for the beneficiary to lease waqf land.

Key Takeaway
Leasing waqf property is permissible unless the waqif specifically prohibited it; the mutawalli has primary authority to lease, and the qadi may intervene only in the mutawalli's absence or refusal of a beneficial lease.

Ruling on the Debris of a Demolished Waqf
Explains handling of demolished waqf debris

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on debris of a demolished waqf, distinguishing between permissible sale and prohibited division.

Core Idea
Debris of a waqf remains waqf property; it must be used for repair, not divided among beneficiaries.

When a waqf building collapses, what happens to its stones and wood? This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq clarifies that the debris is part of the waqf corpus and must be preserved for repair. Only when return to its place is impossible or loss is feared may the judge authorize its sale, with proceeds used for the waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the debris (an-naqḍ) is considered part of the waqf corpus ('ayn). The default ruling is wajib: it must be preserved and used for repair when needed.
2
Locate the evidence (dalīl)
The evidence is the general principle that the waqf corpus belongs to Allah and the beneficiaries have only usufruct. This is supported by the practice of early Muslims and later Hanafi authorities like al-Hidāyah.
No single hadith is quoted; the argument is based on the nature of waqf and necessity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (proof connection)
The proof shows that the debris cannot be owned by beneficiaries, so it cannot be divided. It must serve the waqf's purpose: repair. If repair is impossible, sale is allowed as a substitution (istibdāl) for the waqf's benefit.
4
Note the ikhtilāf (disagreement) on validity of sale
The author notes a dispute among Hanafi scholars: if sale occurs when return is possible, is it invalid (fāsid) or valid with sin? The author leans towards invalidity.
5
Determine the muftā bihī (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position: debris is sold only when return is impossible or loss is feared. The sale must be by judge's order, and proceeds go to repair or replacement of the waqf.
If no replacement is possible, proceeds go to founder's heirs or poor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصرف نقضه إلى عمارته إن احتاج وإلا حفظه للاحتياج ولا يقسمه بين مستحقي الوقف بيان لما انهدم من بناء الوقف وخشبه . والنقض - بالضم - البناء المنقوض والجمع نقوض . وعن الوبري : النقض بالكسر لا غير كذا في المغرب. وذكر في القاموس أولاً أن النقض بالكسر المنقوض وثانياً أنه بالضم ما انتقض من البنيان. وذكر أن الجمع أنقاض ونقوض وفاعل يصرف الحاكم كما صرح به في الهداية لأنه المحدث عنه بقوله «عمرها الحاكم . وقدمنا أنه لا فرق بين المتولي والحاكم في الإجارة والتعمير فكذا في النقض. وقد سوى بين القاضي والمتولي في الحاوي ،القدسي فإن احتاج الوقف إلى عود النقض أعاده الحصول المقصود به، وإن استغنى عنه أمسكه إلى أن يحتاج إلى عمارته، ولا يجوز قسمته بين مستحقي الوقف لأنه جزء من العين ولا حق للموقوف عليهم فيها وإنما حقهم في المنافع والعين حق الله تعالى فلا يصرف لهم غير حقهم. ولم يذكر المصنف بيعه قال في الهداية : وإن تعذر إعادة عينه إلى موضعه بيع وصرف ثمنه إلى المرمة صرفاً للبدل إلى مصرف المبدل اهـ. وظاهره أنه لا يجوز بيعه حيث أمكن إعادته وهل يفسد البيع أو يصح مع إثم المتولي؟ لم أره صريحاً وينبغي الفساد، وقدمنا أنه لا يجوز بيع بعض الموقوف لمرمة الباقي بثمن ما باع. زاد في التتارخانية أن المشتري لو هدم البناء ينبغي عزل الناظر، ولا ينبغي للقاضي أن يأتمن الخائن وسبيله أن يعزله اهـ وفي الحاوي : فإن خيف هلاك النقض باعه الحاكم وأمسك ثمنه لعمارته عند الحاجة .اهـ. فعلى هذا يباع النقض في موضعين عند تعذر عوده وعند خوف هلاكه والمراد ما انهدم من الوقف فلو انهدم الوقف كله فقد سئل عنه قارئ الهداية بقولة سئل عن وقف تهدم ولم يكن له شيء يعمر منه ولا أمكن إجارته ولا تعميره هل تباع أنقاضه من حجر وطوب وخشب؟ أجاب: إن كان الأمر كذلك صح بيعه بأمر الحاكم ويشترى بثمنه وقف مكانه، فإذا لم يكن رده إلى ورثة الواقف إن وجدوا وإلا صرف إلى الفقراء اهـ.
And its debris is spent on its repair if needed, otherwise it is preserved for need, and it is not divided among the beneficiaries of the waqf. Explanation of what has collapsed of the waqf's building and its wood. And 'an-naqḍ' – with a ḍamma – is the demolished building, plural 'nuqūḍ'. And from al-Wabri: 'an-naqḍ' with a kasra only, as in al-Mughrib. And it is mentioned in al-Qāmūs first that 'an-naqḍ' with a kasra is the demolished thing, and second that with a ḍamma it is what has collapsed from the building. And it mentioned that the plural is 'anqāḍ' and 'nuqūḍ'. And the doer is the ruler (al-ḥākim) as stated in al-Hidāyah because he is the one addressed by his saying: 'The ruler made it flourish'. And we have stated that there is no difference between the trustee (al-mutawallī) and the ruler in leasing and repair, and similarly regarding the debris. And in al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī, equality is made between the judge and the trustee. If the waqf needs the debris to return, he returns it to achieve the intended purpose; if it is self-sufficient, he keeps it until needed for repair. And it is not permissible to divide it among the beneficiaries of the waqf because it is part of the 'ayn (corpus), and the beneficiaries have no right in the corpus; their right is only in the usufruct, and the corpus belongs to Allah, so nothing other than their right is given to them. And the author did not mention its sale. In al-Hidāyah it is said: If returning its 'ayn to its place is impossible, it is sold and its price is spent on repair, because the substitute takes the place of the substituted. The apparent meaning is that it is not permissible to sell it when return is possible. And does the sale become invalid (fasād) or valid (ṣaḥīḥ) with sin upon the trustee? I have not seen it explicitly, and it should be invalid (fasād). And we have stated that it is not permissible to sell part of the waqf to repair the remainder with the price of what was sold. In al-Tātārkhāniyyah, it adds: if the buyer demolishes the building, the overseer should be dismissed, and the judge should not trust a treacherous person, and his course is to dismiss him. In al-Ḥāwī: If there is fear of the debris being lost, the judge sells it and holds its price for its repair when needed. Thus, the debris is sold in two situations: when its return is impossible and when there is fear of its loss. And what is meant is what collapsed from the waqf. If the entire waqf collapses, the reader of al-Hidāyah was asked: 'A waqf collapsed and it has nothing to repair it with, nor can it be leased or repaired – may its debris of stone, brick, and wood be sold?' He answered: If that is the case, its sale by order of the judge is valid, and with its price a waqf is purchased in its place. If not, it is returned to the heirs of the founder if they exist, otherwise it is given to the poor.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq explains the legal ruling on the debris (anqāḍ) of a demolished waqf building. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it provides the legal reasoning (ta'līl) for the rules. The core rule: the debris is not to be divided among the beneficiaries; it must be used for the repair of the waqf if needed, or preserved for future need. The author explains the linguistic meaning of 'an-naqḍ', then clarifies that the judge (or the trustee) handles the debris. If the debris cannot be returned to its original place (e.g., due to decay or loss of shape), it may be sold with the judge's permission, and the proceeds are used for repairs. If the entire waqf is ruined and no repair is possible, the debris can be sold to purchase a new waqf property. If that is not possible, the proceeds go to the heirs of the founder, or if none, to the poor. The passage also notes a disagreement: some texts suggest the sale is valid but the trustee may be sinful; the author leans towards the sale being invalid if return is possible. This is from the later Hanafi tradition (mutakhkhirīn) and is consistent with the principle that the corpus ('ayn) of the waqf is inalienable except for necessity.

Key Terms
النقض (an-naqḍ): The demolished materials (debris) of a waqf building, such as stones, bricks, wood.
الاستبدال (al-istibdāl): Selling a waqf property and buying another with the proceeds, permitted only under strict necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When may the debris of a demolished waqf be sold according to the passage?
A) Whenever the beneficiaries wish
B) When returning it to its place is impossible or there is fear of its loss
C) Only when the founder consents
D) Only after ten years of disuse

Key Takeaway
Debris of a demolished waqf must be preserved for repair; sale is only allowed when return is impossible or loss feared, and proceeds must serve the waqf's purpose.

Founder Stipulating Waqf Produce for Himself
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on a founder stipulating waqf produce for himself, identify the proof of each, and explain why the later fatwa follows Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A waqf founder may stipulate the produce for himself because waqf removes ownership to Allah, not to another person; this is the relied-upon view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a waqf founder reserve the benefit (ghallah) of the endowment for himself during his lifetime? The text presents the arguments of Abu Yusuf (who allows it) and Muhammad al-Shaybani (who forbids it), then shows how later authorities weighed the evidence and settled on Abu Yusuf's view to encourage charitable endowments.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify what the founder is stipulating: the produce (ghallah) of the waqf for himself during his life, and/or the trusteeship (wilāyah). Note that the dispute is only about the produce stipulation.
The passage also mentions stipulating wilāyah, but the main dispute is about the ghallah.
2
State the two positions
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds the stipulation is invalid because waqf requires transferring ownership away from oneself. Abu Yusuf holds it is valid because waqf is removal of ownership to Allah, not conveyance to another human.
Both Imams are from the Hanafi school; the dispute is intra-school.
3
Examine Muhammad's proof
Muhammad analogizes the stipulation to giving charity (ṣadaqah) to oneself, which is impossible. Waqf, like charity, must be for others. He also compares it to stipulating a part of a mosque for personal use.
The analogy is qiyas on a similar prohibition.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf cites the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ate from his own charity (interpreted as endowed charity), implying stipulation made it permissible. He also argues that waqf is a devotion to Allah, so stipulating personal use is like building a caravanserai with condition to stay in it.
The Prophet's practice is a stronger proof (naqlī) than mere analogy.
5
Analyze the tarjih
Later authorities like al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd, scholars of Balkh, and the author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq prefer Abu Yusuf's view. The fatwa is given accordingly to encourage people to establish waqfs.
The tarjih is based on maslahah (public interest) and the strength of the naqlī proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن جعل الواقف غلة الوقف لنفسه أو جعل الولاية إليه صح أي لو شرط عند الإيقاف ذلك اعتبر شرطه ؛ أما الأول فهو جائز عند أبي يوسف ولا يجوز على قياس قول محمد من اشتراط التسليم إلى المتولي عنده . وقيل : إن الاختلاف بينهما بناء على اشتراط القبض والإفراز . وقيل : هي مسألة مبتدأة فالخلاف فيما إذا شرط البعض لنفسه في حياته وبعد موته للفقراء، وفيما إذا شرط الكل لنفسه في حياته وبعده للفقراء. وجه قول محمد أن الوقف شرع على وجه التمليك بالطريق الذي قدمناه فاشتراطه الكل أو البعض لنفسه يبطله لأن التمليك من نفسه لا يتحقق فصار كالصدقة المنفذة وشرط بعض بقعة المسجد لنفسه. ولأبي يوسف ما روي أن النبي كان يأكل من ،صدقته، والمراد منها صدقته الموقوفة ولا يحل الأكل منه إلا بالشرط فدل على صحته ولأن الوقف إزالة الملك إلى الله تعالى على وجه القبة على ما بيناه فإذا شرط البعض أو الكل لنفسه فقد جعل ما صار مملوكاً الله تعالى لنفسه لا ان يجعل ملك نفسه لنفسه وهذا جائز كما إذا بنى خاناً أو سقاية أو جعل أرضه مقبرة وشرط أن يـ له أو يشرب منه أو يدفن فيه، ولأن مقصوده القربة وفي الصرف إلى نفسه ذلك قال عليه السلام نفقة الرجل على نفسه صدقة». وفي فتح القدير : فقد ترجح قول أبي يوسف : قال الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. ونحن أيضاً نفتي بقوله ترغيباً للناس في الوقف واختاره مشايخ بلخ، وكذا ظاهر الهداية حيث أخر وجهه ولم يدفعه. ومن صور الاشتراط لنفسه ما لو قال أن يقضي دينه من غلته، وكذا إذا قال إذا حدث على الموت وعلى دين يبدأ من غلة هذا الوقف بقضاء ما علي فما فضل فعلى سبيله كل. ذلك جائز. وفي وقف الخصاف : فإذا شرط أن ينفق على نفسه وولده وحشمه وعياله من عدم فيه قوله : (فعلى هذا يباع النقض في موضعين يزاد عليهما ما في الفتح حيث قال : واعلم أن . جواز بيعه إلا إذا تعذر الانتفاع به إنما هو فيما ورد عليه وقف الواقف أما فيما اشتراه المتولي من مستغلات الوقف فإنه يجوز بيعه بلا هذا الشرط. وهذا لأن في صيرورته وقفاً خلافاً، والمختار أنه لا
And if the founder makes the produce of the waqf for himself or makes the trusteeship for himself, it is valid – i.e., if he stipulates that at the time of endowment, his condition is observed. As for the first (stipulating produce for himself), it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and not permissible by analogy with the view of Muhammad regarding stipulating delivery to the trustee. And it is said that the difference between them is based on stipulating possession and segregation. And it is said: it is a new issue; the disagreement is when he stipulates part for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, and when he stipulates all for himself during his life and after his death for the poor. The basis of Muhammad's view is that waqf is legislated as a form of ownership (tamleek) in the manner we have explained, so stipulating all or part for himself invalidates it because ownership from oneself is not realized, so it becomes like a direct charity (ṣadaqah munfadhah) and stipulating a part of the mosque for himself. For Abu Yusuf, there is the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to eat from his charity, meaning his endowed charity, and it is not halal to eat from it except by stipulation, so that indicates its validity. And because waqf is the removal of ownership to Allah Almighty as an act of devotion (qurbah) as we have explained; so if he stipulates part or all for himself, he has made what became owned by Allah for himself – not that he makes his own property for himself – and this is permissible, just as if he builds a caravanserai, a drinking fountain, or makes his land a cemetery and stipulates that he may stay in it, drink from it, or be buried in it. And because his purpose is devotion, and in spending on himself there is devotion as the Prophet said: 'A man's spending on himself is charity.' In Fatḥ al-Qadīr: the view of Abu Yusuf is preponderant. Al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd said: the fatwa is on the view of Abu Yusuf. And we also give fatwa according to his view to encourage people to make endowments, and it was chosen by the scholars of Balkh. Similarly, the apparent meaning of al-Hidāyah is that it delayed his proof and did not refute it. Among the forms of stipulating for himself: if he says that his debt should be paid from its produce, and likewise if he says: 'If death occurs and there is a debt, it should begin from the produce of this waqf to pay what I owe, and whatever remains is as it was.' All that is permissible. In Waqf al-Khaṣṣāf: If he stipulates that he spends on himself, his children, his servants, and his household from ...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a founder (wāqif) stipulating that the produce (ghallah) of the waqf be for himself during his lifetime, or that he retains the trusteeship (wilāyah). The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. According to Abu Yusuf, such a stipulation is valid; the founder may reserve the benefit for himself. Muhammad says it is invalid because waqf requires transferring ownership away from oneself completely. The text provides Abu Yusuf's proofs: first, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) eating from his own charity (understood as waqf), implying that stipulation makes it permissible; second, waqf is a removal of ownership to Allah, so stipulating benefit for oneself is akin to building a public facility with conditions for personal use. The commentary in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq then notes that the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, as adopted by later authorities like al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd and the scholars of Balkh, and even al-Hidāyah implies acceptance. The passage also gives practical examples: the founder can stipulate that his debts be paid from the waqf's produce. The last part of the OCR is garbled, but it seems to discuss a different ruling about selling debris. The key takeaway: the Hanafi school, in its later fatwa, permits the founder to reserve benefit for himself to encourage waqf endowments.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghallah): The produce, income, or usufruct of the waqf property (e.g., rent from a building).
الولاية (al-wilāyah): The authority (guardianship or trusteeship) over the waqf, normally held by the trustee (mutawallī).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The stipulation is valid and the founder may take the produce
C) The stipulation is valid only if the produce is given to the poor after his death
D) The stipulation is valid only with court approval

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a waqf founder to stipulate the produce for himself, and this is the preferred view adopted for fatwa to encourage endowments.

Selling the Debris of a Ruined Waqf
Ruling on when and how to sell the debris of a waqf that has collapsed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which the debris of a ruined waqf may be sold and explain the procedure when the entire waqf collapses.

Core Idea
Debris of a collapsed waqf is sold only when reuse is impossible or destruction feared, preserving the endowment.

Waqf property is inalienable in principle, but when a waqf building collapses, its debris (naqḍ) poses a legal question: can it be sold? Hanafi jurists permit sale only under specific conditions to protect the waqf's purpose. In this passage, the author from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the two scenarios for selling debris and the fatwa of Qari al-Hidayah on complete destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions
From the quoted sources (al-Hawi), extract the two situations where the sale of debris is allowed: when the debris cannot be reused in the waqf (تعذر عوده) and when its destruction is feared (خوف هلاكه).
These are the only two valid reasons for sale.
2
Examine the rationale
Why does the law restrict sale to these two situations? Consider the waqf's perpetuity: the purpose is to preserve the endowment. Sale is a last resort when the debris cannot serve the waqf or is at risk of being lost.
3
Apply to complete collapse
When the entire waqf collapses, proceed stepwise: first, sell debris by judge's order and buy a new waqf property; if not possible, return proceeds to founder's heirs; if no heirs, give to the poor.
This hierarchy ensures the waqf's objective is fulfilled as far as possible.
4
Note the role of the judge
Court permission is required in all cases. The judge ensures the conditions are met, the sale is at fair value, and proceeds are properly managed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتولي؟ لم أره صريحاً وينبغي الفساد، وقدمنا أنه لا يجوز بيع بعض الموقوف لمرمة الباقي بثمن ما باع. زاد في التتارخانية أن المشتري لو هدم البناء ينبغي عزل الناظر، ولا ينبغي للقاضي أن يأتمن الخائن وسبيله أن يعزله اهـ وفي الحاوي : فإن خيف هلاك النقض باعه الحاكم وأمسك ثمنه لعمارته عند الحاجة .اهـ. فعلى هذا يباع النقض في موضعين عند تعذر عوده وعند خوف هلاكه والمراد ما انهدم من الوقف فلو انهدم الوقف كله فقد سئل عنه قارئ الهداية بقولة سئل عن وقف تهدم ولم يكن له شيء يعمر منه ولا أمكن إجارته ولا تعميره هل تباع أنقاضه من حجر وطوب وخشب؟ أجاب: إن كان الأمر كذلك صح بيعه بأمر الحاكم ويشترى بثمنه وقف مكانه، فإذا لم يكن رده إلى ورثة الواقف إن وجدوا وإلا صرف إلى الفقراء اهـ.
The trustee? I did not see it explicitly, and it should be invalid. And we previously stated that it is not permissible to sell part of the endowed property to repair the remainder with the price of what was sold. Added in al-Tatar Khaniyya: if the buyer demolishes the building, the trustee should be removed, and it is not befitting for the judge to trust the treacherous one, and his path is to remove him. End. In al-Hawi: If destruction of the debris is feared, the judge sells it and holds its price for its repair when needed. End. So on this basis, the debris is sold in two situations: when its restoration is impossible and when its destruction is feared. What is meant is what has collapsed from the waqf. If the entire waqf collapses, Qari al-Hidayah was asked: A waqf collapsed and it has nothing with which to repair it, nor can it be leased or repaired. Can its debris of stone, brick, and wood be sold? He answered: If such is the case, its sale is valid with the judge's order, and with its price a waqf is purchased in its place; if not, it is returned to the heirs of the founder if they exist, otherwise it is given to the poor. End.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on selling the debris of a ruined waqf. The author first quotes a question about the trustee's role, then cites al-Tatar Khaniyya that a dishonest trustee should be removed. He then references al-Hawi: if the debris is at risk of being ruined, the judge may sell it and keep the price for future repairs. The main ruling is that debris is sold only in two cases: (1) when it cannot be reused in the waqf (e.g., the walls are too damaged), and (2) when it is feared that the debris itself will be destroyed (e.g., due to weather). The passage then presents a fatwa from Qari al-Hidayah regarding a completely destroyed waqf: the judge may sell the debris and use the proceeds to buy a new waqf property. If that is not possible, the money goes to the founder's heirs, or if none, to the poor. This ensures the waqf's purpose is preserved as much as possible.

Key Terms
نقض (naqḍ): Debris or demolished parts of a waqf structure (stone, wood, brick).
وقف (waqf): Endowment of property for charitable purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only when the judge gives permission unconditionally
D) When the trustee needs money for personal expenses

Key Takeaway
Waqf debris may be sold only when reuse is impossible or destruction feared, preserving the endowment for its intended purpose.

The Founder's Stipulation of Waqf Produce for Himself: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a founder stipulating the produce of his waqf for himself, evaluate the proofs of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
The founder may validly stipulate the produce of his waqf for himself; the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf to encourage endowments.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a key internal Hanafi dispute on whether a waqf founder can reserve the produce (ghullah) for his own benefit. The matn states it is valid, but the commentary reveals a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute is essential for anyone dealing with waqf formation in Hanafi fiqh, as the relied-upon position has practical implications for endowment planning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is whether the founder's stipulation that the waqf's produce (ghullah) be given to himself during his lifetime is valid. The matn briefly states it is valid; the commentary expands on the disagreement.
2
State Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad prohibits it because waqf is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) to Allah, and one cannot transfer ownership to oneself. His analogy is with a charity that takes immediate effect and then the donor takes it back (executed charity).
He compares it to 'stipulating a spot of the mosque for oneself.'
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf permits it based on the hadith of the Prophet eating from his own sadaqah (interpreted as waqf) and the analogy of building a public facility (khan, watering trough) while reserving its use for oneself. Waqf removes ownership to Allah; the stipulation is a condition, not self-transfer.
4
Identify the tarjih and mufta bihi
Later scholars (Fath al-Qadir, al-Sadr al-Shahid, scholars of Balkh) prefer Abu Yusuf's view. The fatwa is given accordingly to encourage people to make waqf. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq also affirms this.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
The passage applies the dispute to paying debts from the waqf produce, supporting family, and even waqf on slaves. The mufta bihi position allows these stipulations. The dispute's thamarah (practical consequence) is that waqf becomes more flexible and attractive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن جعل الواقف غلة الوقف لنفسه أو جعل الولاية إليه صح) أي لو شرط عند الإيقاف ذلك اعتبر شرطه ؛ أما الأول فهو جائز عند أبي يوسف ولا يجوز على قياس قول محمد من اشتراط التسليم إلى المتولي عنده . وقيل : إن الاختلاف بينهما بناء على اشتراط القبض والإفراز . وقيل : هي مسألة مبتدأة فالخلاف فيما إذا شرط البعض لنفسه في حياته وبعد موته للفقراء، وفيما إذا شرط الكل لنفسه في حياته وبعده للفقراء. وجه قول محمد أن الوقف شرع على وجه التمليك بالطريق الذي قدمناه فاشتراطه الكل أو البعض لنفسه يبطله لأن التمليك من نفسه لا يتحقق فصار كالصدقة المنفذة وشرط بعض بقعة المسجد لنفسه. ولأبي يوسف ما روي أن النبي كان يأكل من ،صدقته، والمراد منها صدقته الموقوفة ولا يحل الأكل منه إلا بالشرط فدل على صحته ولأن الوقف إزالة الملك إلى الله تعالى على وجه القبة على ما بيناه فإذا شرط البعض أو الكل لنفسه فقد جعل ما صار مملوكاً الله تعالى لنفسه لا ان يجعل ملك نفسه لنفسه وهذا جائز كما إذا بنى خاناً أو سقاية أو جعل أرضه مقبرة وشرط أن يـ له أو يشرب منه أو يدفن فيه، ولأن مقصوده القربة وفي الصرف إلى نفسه ذلك قال عليه السلام نفقة الرجل على نفسه صدقة». وفي فتح القدير : فقد ترجح قول أبي يوسف : قال الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. ونحن أيضاً نفتي بقوله ترغيباً للناس في الوقف واختاره مشايخ بلخ، وكذا ظاهر الهداية حيث أخر وجهه ولم يدفعه. ومن صور الاشتراط لنفسه ما لو قال أن يقضي دينه من غلته، وكذا إذا قال إذا حدث على الموت وعلى دين يبدأ من غلة هذا الوقف بقضاء ما علي فما فضل فعلى سبيله كل. ذلك جائز. وفي وقف الخصاف : فإذا شرط أن ينفق على نفسه وولده وحشمه وعياله من غلة هذا الوقف فجاءت غلته فباعها وقبض ثمنها ثم مات قبل أن ينفق ذلك، هل يكون ذلك لورثته أو لأهل الوقف؟ قال : يكون لورثته لأنه قد حصل ذلك وكان له، فقد عرف أن شرط بعض الغلة لا يلزم كونه بعضاً معيناً كالنصف والربع، وكذلك إذا قال إن حدث على فلان الموت يعني الواقف نفسه أخرج من غلة هذا الوقف في كل سنة من عشرة أسهم مثلاً سهم يجعل في الحج عنه أو في كفارة أيمانه وفي كذا وكذا وسمى أشياء أو قال اخرج من هذه الصدقة في كل سنة كذا وكذا درهماً ليصرف في هذه الوجوه ويصرف الباقي في كذا وكذا على ما سبله .اهـ. وفي الحاوي القدسي : المختار للفتوى قول أبي يوسف ترغيباً للناس في الوقف وتكثيراً للخير ويتفرع على هذا الاختلاف أيضاً ما لو وقف على عبيده وإمائه؛ فعند محمد لا يجوز، وعند أبي يوسف يجوز كشرطه لنفسه. وفرع بعضهم عليه أيضاً اشتراط الغلة لمدبريه وأمهات أولاده وهو ضعيف، والأصح أنه اتفاقاً. والفرق لمحمد أن صحيح حريتهم ثبتت بموته فيكون الوقف عليهم كالوقف على الأجانب ويكون ثبوته لهم حال حياته تبعاً لما بعد موته، فما في الهداية والمجتبى من تصحيح أنها على الخلاف ضعيف.
His statement: (If the founder makes the produce of the waqf for himself or makes the trusteeship to himself, it is valid.) That is, if he stipulates that upon endowment, his condition is considered. As for the first, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf and not permissible on the analogy of Muhammad's statement regarding stipulating delivery to the trustee according to him. And it is said: the difference between them is based on stipulating possession and segregation. And it is said: it is an independent issue; the disagreement is when he stipulates part for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, and when he stipulates all for himself during his life and after his death for the poor. The reasoning of Muhammad's statement is that waqf is legislated on the basis of ownership transfer in the manner we have stated, so stipulating all or part for himself invalidates it because ownership from oneself is not realized, so it becomes like a executed charity and stipulating some spot of the mosque for himself. For Abu Yusuf, he uses the narration that the Prophet used to eat from his sadaqah, and what is meant is his endowed sadaqah, and eating from it is not permissible except by stipulation, so it indicates its validity. And because waqf is removal of ownership to Allah Almighty on the basis of nearness as we have explained, so if he stipulates part or all for himself, he has made what became owned by Allah Almighty for himself, not that he is making his own ownership for himself, and this is permissible just as if he built a khan or a watering trough or made his land a cemetery and stipulated that he eats from it or drinks from it or is buried in it. And because his purpose is piety, and spending on oneself is included in that: the Prophet said, 'A man's spending on himself is charity.' In Fath al-Qadir: the view of Abu Yusuf has preponderance. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement. And we also give fatwa by his statement to encourage people to make waqf, and the scholars of Balkh chose it, and likewise the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah where it deferred his reasoning and did not refute it. Among the forms of stipulation for oneself: if he says that his debt be paid from its produce, and likewise if he says: when death occurs to me, and I have a debt, begin from the produce of this waqf to pay what is upon me, and what remains is on its way. All that is permissible. In Waqf al-Khassaf: if he stipulates that he spend on himself, his children, his servants, and his dependents from the produce of this waqf, then its produce comes and he sells it and takes its price, then dies before spending it, is it for his heirs or for the people of the waqf? He said: it is for his heirs because it was acquired and belonged to him. So it is known that stipulating part of the produce does not require it to be a specific part like half or quarter. Similarly, if he says: when death occurs to so-and-so, meaning the founder himself, take out from the produce of this waqf every year, for example, one out of ten shares, to be used for hajj on his behalf, or for expiation of his oaths, and such and such, and he specified things, or he said: take out from this charity every year such and such dirhams to be spent on these purposes, and spend the remainder on such and such according to his specification. End. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: the chosen for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's statement to encourage people to make waqf and increase good. And derived from this disagreement is also if he endows upon his male and female slaves: according to Muhammad it is not permissible, according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible like his stipulation for himself. And some derived from it also stipulating the produce for his mudabbars and ummahat awlad, but that is weak; the correct view is that it is agreed upon. The distinction for Muhammad is that their freedom is established only upon his death, so the waqf upon them is like waqf upon strangers, and its establishment for them during his life is subsidiary to after his death. So what is in al-Hidayah and al-Mujtaba that it is based on disagreement is weak.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents a major intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the founder of a waqf may stipulate that he himself receives the produce (غلة) of the waqf during his lifetime. The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states that such a stipulation is valid. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym?) explains that it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, but not on the analogy of Muhammad's view. Two explanations are given for the divergence: one ties it to the requirement of possession and segregation (قبض وإفراز); another sees it as an independent issue. Muhammad argues that waqf is a transfer of ownership, so the founder cannot transfer ownership to himself; it would be like a charity that is executed but the founder takes back. Abu Yusuf relies on a hadith that the Prophet would eat from his own sadaqah (interpreted as his waqf), indicating that such a stipulation is valid. He also argues that waqf removes ownership to Allah, and the founder can then take from it by condition, analogous to building a public facility and reserving use for himself. The commentator notes that Fath al-Qadir, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and the scholars of Balkh all prefer Abu Yusuf's view, and the fatwa is based on it to encourage waqf. The passage then details practical applications: using the produce to pay debts, support family, etc. It also extends the dispute to waqf on slaves and mudabbars, with the preferred view that it is allowed. The author concludes by critiquing the claim in al-Hidayah that the issue of slaves is based on disagreement, saying it is weak.

Key Terms
غلة (ghullah): The produce or revenue generated by the waqf property (e.g., rent, crop yield).
اشتراط القبض والإفراز (ishtirāṭ al-qabḍ wa al-ifrāz): Stipulation that the waqf must be delivered into the possession of the trustee and segregated from the founder's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mufta bihi position allows the waqf founder to stipulate the produce for himself during his lifetime, based on the hadith of the Prophet and to encourage endowments.

Waqf on Oneself: Ruling and Scholarly Critique
Ruling on waqf on oneself with critical exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on waqf on oneself and explain the critical disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf, and evaluate the scholarly response to claims of weakness.

Core Idea
Waqf on oneself is valid (ja'iz) per Abu Yusuf and the mufta bihi, despite some claims of weakness.

Waqf is a perpetual charitable endowment, but what if the founder stipulates that he himself benefits from its produce during his lifetime? This lesson delves into the Hanafi ruling on this practice (الوقف على النفس). You will navigate the primary dispute between Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf and Abu Yusuf, examine a later commentator's criticism of the minority view, and understand why the relied-upon position favors validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is the ruling when a founder makes a waqf and stipulates that its produce is for himself during his lifetime? This is the core issue of 'waqf on oneself'.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two notable early Hanafi opinions: Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf rules it invalid; Abu Yusuf rules it valid. Identify the basis for each (e.g., requirements of perpetuity and separation).
3
Analyze the critical refinement
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) dismisses the validity view as weak. Then al-Ramli refutes this, arguing that the view is not necessarily weak because it may be independent of another dispute (possession and segregation). Understand the layers of critique.
Pay attention to 'وَلَعَلَّهُ جَعَلَ' and the rebuttal.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'المعتمد صحة الوقف على النفس' – the relied-upon is validity. Identify the authority (Abu Yusuf) and the later scholars who uphold it (e.g., al-Ramli).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Use the scenarios from al-Khaniyyah (e.g., founder includes himself and another, or himself and descendants) to test the ruling's boundaries and see which parts are considered valid or invalid.

قيد بجعل الغلة لنفسه لأنه لو وقف على نفسه. قال أبو بكر الإسكاف لا يجوز وعن أبي يوسف جوازه. وإذا مات صار إلى المساكين ولو قال أرضى صدقة موقوفة على أن لي غلتها ما عشت قال هلال لا يجوز هذا الوقف. وذكر الأنصاري جوازه. وإذا مات يكون للفقراء ؛ كذا في الخانية. وفيها : لو وقف وقفاً واستثنى لنفسه أن يأكل . منه ما دام حياً ثم مات وعنده هذا الوقف معاليق عنب أو زبيب فذلك كله مردود إلى الوقف ولو كان عنده خبز من من بر ذلك الوقف يكون ميراثاً لأن ذلك ليس من الوقف حقيقة .اهـ. وحاصله أن المعتمد صحة الوقف على النفس واشتراط أن تكون الغلة له فما في الخانية من أنه لو وقف على نفسه وعلى فلان نصفه حصة فلان وبطل حصة نفسه، ولو قال على نفسي ثم على فلان وهو أو قال على فلان ثم على نفسي لا يصح شيء منه، ولو قال على عبدي وعلى فلان صح في النصف وبطل في النصف، ولو قال على نفسي وولدي ونسلي فالوقف كله باطل لأن حصة النسل مجهولة .اهـ. مبني على القول الضعيف، والعجب کیف جزم به وساقه على طريقة صح منه يكون وقفاً فللقيم أن يبيعه متى شاء لمصلحة عرضت اهـ قوله : (والعجب منه كيف جزم به الخ) قال الرملي أقول : كيف يتجه له القطع بكونه ضعيفاً وقد قدم في شرح قوله «ولا يتم» أن أكثر فقهاء الأمصار أخذوا بقول محمد وأن الفتوى عليه، فالعجب ممن وصفه بالضعف مع ما يقضي بوصف القوة تأمل اهـ . قلت : لا يلزم من إفتائهم بقول محمد بلزوم القبض والإفراز إفتاؤهم بقوله بعدم صحة الوقف على النفس، ولاسيما إن قلنا أنه مسألة مبتدأة غير مبنية على اشتراط القبض والإفراز لكن لم يذكر المؤلف ما يدل على تصحيح قول أبي يوسف في صحة الوقف على النفس ولعله جعل البحر الرائق/ ج ٥/ ٢٤٥
Restricted to making the produce for himself because if he makes a waqf on himself. Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf said: it is not permissible, and from Abu Yusuf its permissibility. And when he dies it goes to the poor. And if he said: 'My land is a sadaqah waqf on the condition that its produce is for me as long as I live,' Hilal said: this waqf is not permissible. And al-Ansari mentioned its permissibility. And when he dies it is for the poor. Likewise in al-Khaniyyah. And in it: If he made a waqf and excluded for himself that he eats from it as long as he lives, then he died and with him from this waqf there are clusters of grapes or raisins, all that is returned to the waqf. And if he had bread from the wheat of that waqf, it would be inheritance because that is not actually from the waqf. End. The summary is that the relied-upon position is the validity of waqf on oneself and stipulating that the produce is for himself. So what is in al-Khaniyyah that if he made a waqf on himself and on someone else, half is valid for the other and the share of himself is invalid; and if he said 'on myself then on so-and-so' or 'on so-and-so then on myself', nothing of it is valid; and if he said 'on my slave and on so-and-so', half is valid and half invalid; and if he said 'on myself, my children, and my descendants', the entire waqf is invalid because the share of the descendants is unknown. End. It is based on the weak opinion, and it is surprising that he was categorical about it and presented it as if it were correct. Then from it, it becomes waqf, so the trustee may sell it whenever he wishes for an interest that arises. End. His statement: (And it is surprising that he was categorical about it etc.) Al-Ramli said: I say: How can he be certain that it is weak, when he previously stated in the commentary on 'wa la yatimmu' that most jurists of the regions took Muhammad's statement and the fatwa is upon it. So surprising is the one who describes it as weak when there is that which indicates its strength. Reflect. End. I say: It does not necessarily follow from their giving fatwa on Muhammad's statement regarding the necessity of possession and segregation that they give fatwa on his statement regarding the invalidity of waqf on oneself, especially if we say it is an independent issue not built on the stipulation of possession and segregation. But the author did not mention anything indicating the correction of Abu Yusuf's statement on the validity of waqf on oneself, and perhaps he made it (the sea) the beacon? End.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on making a waqf where the founder himself is the beneficiary (الوقف على النفس), which is distinct from merely reserving the produce. The author notes that Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf deemed it invalid, while Abu Yusuf permitted it. The relied-upon view is that such a waqf is valid, with the produce for the founder during his life and then for the poor after death. The text from al-Khaniyyah presents several scenarios: if the founder makes the waqf on himself and another, the other's share is valid; if the order is 'on myself then on so-and-so', the entire waqf is invalid; and so on. The author of the original commentary (likely Ibn Nujaym) then criticizes this presentation, calling it based on a weak opinion. However, al-Ramli responds that describing the view as weak is itself problematic, since many scholars follow Muhammad in requiring possession and segregation, but that does not automatically invalidate waqf on oneself. The passage ends with the commentator (possibly the author of the hashiya) defending the possibility that the issue of waqf on oneself is independent and not necessarily tied to the earlier dispute about possession. The final line 'ولعله جعل البحر الرائق' is ambiguous but may refer to the author's own work.

Key Terms
الوقف على النفس (al-waqf 'ala al-nafs): Endowment where the founder himself is the beneficiary of the produce/usufruct.
معاليق (ma'ālīq): Clusters of grapes or raisins that are hung.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a waqf where the founder himself is the beneficiary (الوقف على النفس) according to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school?
A) It is invalid according to all Hanafi scholars
B) It is valid according to Abu Yusuf and that is the mufta bihi
C) It is valid only if the produce is for the founder's children
D) It is invalid because the founder cannot be both donor and recipient

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that waqf on oneself is valid (ja'iz), following Abu Yusuf; the produce is for the founder during life and then for the poor after death.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
10 min
Waqif Stipulating Produce for Himself: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif's self-benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on a waqif's stipulation of benefit for himself, explain the tarjih mechanism, and apply the mufta bihi to similar cases.

Core Idea
A waqif may stipulate the produce for himself; Abu Yusuf's view is mufta bihi to encourage waqf.

Imagine a person endows his garden as a waqf but stipulates that he may keep the fruit for himself during his lifetime. Is this valid? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it invalid, arguing that one cannot benefit from one's own charity. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, permits it, reasoning that it encourages people to establish endowments. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the practical consequences, and why later scholars preferred Abu Yusuf's view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi positions
State the two competing views within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf's permissibility and Muhammad's prohibition regarding the waqif taking produce from his own waqf during his lifetime.
Abu Hanifa's explicit view is absent, but he generally supports facilitation.
2
Examine the reasoning of each imam
Abu Yusuf's dalil is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the public interest (maslahah) of encouraging waqf. Muhammad's dalil is that waqf removes ownership, so the waqif cannot subsequently benefit from the endowed property.
The source text implies Muhammad's view is like 'selling ownership' to oneself.
3
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if valid, the waqif can lawfully consume or use the produce; if invalid, the condition is void, and if the waqf itself is conditional upon it, the entire waqf may be void.
The text mentions that if waqf on oneself with a stipulation is invalid (Muhammad), the waqf fails; if valid (Abu Yusuf), it stands.
4
Determine the tarjih and its basis
Later Hanafi authorities like al-Hawi al-Qudsi and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq preferred Abu Yusuf's view, making it mufta bihi. The rationale is to encourage people to endow property (targhiban li al-nas fi al-waqf).
This is a classic example of tarjih through maslahah, even though the alternative is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Apply the settled view to branch cases
Extend the ruling to similar scenarios: waqf on one's slaves, mudabbars, or oneself with specific beneficiaries. The text notes that some branches are weak and the correct opinion is that the same dispute applies.
Be cautious: the text warns that treating some branches as agreed-upon may be erroneous.

Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage combines a specific ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a waqif stipulating benefit (ghalla) for himself during his lifetime. The opening case establishes that the income from a waqf, once sold and collected, becomes owned by the waqif and passes to his heirs if he dies before spending it. The author then discusses conditions that allow the waqif to take a portion of the produce for specific purposes. The core dispute: Abu Yusuf permits the waqif to stipulate the produce for himself, while Muhammad al-Shaybani and others hold it invalid. The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) according to al-Hawi al-Qudsi is Abu Yusuf's view, to encourage waqf. The text then branches into related issues: waqf on one's own slaves (where the same dispute applies), the opinion of Abu Bakr al-Isfaf and others. The author concludes that the reliable position is the validity of waqf on oneself with stipulation of benefit, despite some texts showing disagreement. The commentary by al-Ramli criticizes a scholar for dismissing this view as weak. Students should note that the authority weight here is mixed: the dispute involves founding imams, but the mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's, which is from the Nawadir or later Fatawa, while Muhammad's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The text reflects a later preference for facilitation.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghallah): The produce or income generated from the waqf property, which the waqif may stipulate for himself or for others.
الوقف على النفس (al-waqf 'ala al-nafs): An endowment where the waqif designates benefit for himself during his lifetime.
المختار للفتوى (al-mukhtar li al-fatwa): The chosen opinion for issuing fatwas, which in this case is Abu Yusuf's view.

C) Only valid if written

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school allows a waqif to stipulate the produce of the waqf for himself during his lifetime, based on Abu Yusuf's view to encourage waqf.

Waqf — Endowment

Hanafi Rules of Waqf on Children and Grandchildren
Series of rulings on waqf for children and grandchildren

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for waqf on children, including when 'walad' includes both sexes, when grandchildren are excluded, and how distribution works across generations.

Core Idea
In Hanafi waqf, 'walad' includes sons and daughters; grandchildren are excluded unless specifically named.

Waqf (endowment) on family members is a common practice, but its precise legal effects depend on the words used. This lesson presents the core Hanafi rulings on who benefits when a waqf is made on 'children' (walad) or 'sons' (banin), including subtle rules about grandchildren and multiple generations. Understanding these rules ensures that the endowment achieves the waqif's intent and avoids common errors.

Guided Path
1
Primacy of spoken conditions
The waqf is enforced based on what the waqif spoke, not what the scribe wrote. Any proven spoken condition overrides the document.
This principle appears early in the passage and sets the foundation.
2
Define 'walad' in waqf context
When the waqf is on 'walad' (child), it includes both male and female offspring unless the waqif specifically restricts it to males (e.g., 'banin').
The term 'ibn' is male-specific; 'walad' is gender-neutral in this context.
3
Rule for grandchildren
Grandchildren (walad al-walad) receive nothing if a direct child exists. If no child, the son's child takes. Daughters' children are excluded in the apparent narration unless special conditions.
Note the difference between son's child (enters if no child) and daughter's child (generally excluded).
4
Distribution across generations
If only one generation is named, after the last beneficiary dies, the waqf goes to the poor. If three generations (butun) are named, the waqf continues as long as any descendant exists, even downwards.
This is a key rule that determines perpetuity.
5
Differentiate 'awlad' from 'banin'
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Khaniyyah treats 'awlad' (children) and 'banin' (sons) equally – a single child takes all. Fath al-Qadir differentiates: 'awlad' – one takes all; 'banin' – one takes half, half to poor. The mufta bihi is the equality view.
This dispute affects the share of a single beneficiary.

ثم اعلم أن الاعتبار في الشروط لما تكلم به الواقف لا لما كتب في مكتوب الوقف، فلو أقيمت بينة بشرط تكلم به الواقف ولم يوجد في المكتوب عمل به لما في البزازية : وقد أشرنا أن الوقف على ما تكلم به لا على ما كتب الكاتب فيدخل في الوقف المذكور وغير المذكور في الصك أعني كل ما تكلم به .اهـ ولا خلاف في اشتراط الغلة لولده فإذا وقف على ولده شمل الذكر والأنثى، وإن قيده بالذكر لا تدخل الأنثى كالابن. ولا شيء لولد الولد مع وجود الولد فإن لم يوجد له ولد كانت لولد الابن. ولا يدخل ولد البنت في الوقف على الولد مفرداً وجمعاً في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح المفتى به . ولو وقف على ولده وولد ولده اشترك ولده وولد ابنه. وصحح قاضيخان دخول أولاد البنات فيما إذا وقف على أولاده وأولاد أولاده، وصحح عدمه في ولدي. ولو قال على ولدي فمات كانت للفقراء ولا تصرف إلى ولد ولده في كل بطن إلا بالشرط إلا إذا ذكر البطون الثلاثة فإنها لا تصرف إلى الفقراء ما بقي أحد من أولاده وإن سفل. ولو وقف على ولديه ثم على أولادهما فمات أحدهما كان للآخر النصف ونصف الميت للفقراء لا لولده فإذا مات الآخر صرف الكل إلى أولاد الأولاد. ولو وقف على ولده وليس له إلا ولد ابن كانت له، فإن حدث له ولد كانت له ولو وقف على محتاجي ولده وليس له إلا ولد محتاج كان النصف له والآخر للفقراء. ولو وقف على أولاده فماتوا إلا واحداً كان الكل له لا للفقراء إلا بعد موته، ولو عين الأولاد فكل من مات كان نصيبه للفقراء لا لأخواته بغير شرط ولو وقف على أولاده وليس له إلا واحد أو على بنيه وليس له إلا ابن واحد كان النصف له والنصف للفقراء. هكذا سوى بين الأولاد والأبناء في الخانية، وفرق بينهما في فتح القدير فقال في الأولاد: يستحق الواحد الكل وفي البنين لا يستحق الكل وقال : كأنه مبني على العرف، وقد علمت أن المنقول خلافه. ولو وقف على بنيه لا تستحق البنات كعكسه. وبقية التفاريع المتعلقة بالوقف على الأولاد والأقارب معلومة في الخصاف وغيره
Then know that consideration in conditions is according to what the waqif spoke, not according to what is written in the waqf document. So if evidence is established of a condition spoken by the waqif and it is not found in the document, it is acted upon, as in al-Bazzaziyyah: 'We have indicated that the waqf is upon what is spoken, not upon what the scribe writes, so both mentioned and unmentioned in the deed enter the waqf, meaning everything he spoke.' End. There is no disagreement in stipulating the produce for his child. So if he makes a waqf on his child, it includes male and female. If he restricts it to males, the female does not enter, like the son. There is nothing for the child's child in the presence of the child; if he has no child, it is for the son's child. The daughter's child does not enter in the waqf on 'walad' (child) in singular and plural in the apparent narration, and it is the correct and fatwa position. If he makes a waqf on his child and his child's child, his child and his son's child share. Qadikhan corrected the entry of daughters' children when he makes a waqf on his children and his children's children, and corrected its non-entry in 'my child'. If he said 'on my child' and he died, it is for the poor, and it is not given to his child's child in each generation except by condition, unless he mentioned the three generations, then it is not given to the poor as long as any of his children remain, even if downwards. If he makes a waqf on his two children, then on their children, and one of them dies, the other gets half, and half of the deceased is for the poor, not for his child. Then when the other dies, all is given to the children's children. If he makes a waqf on his child and he has only a son's child, it is for him; if he later gets a child, it becomes for him. If he makes a waqf on the needy of his child and he has only one needy child, half is for him and the other for the poor. If he makes a waqf on his children and they all die except one, all is for him, not for the poor except after his death. If he specifies the children, then whoever dies, his share is for the poor, not for his siblings without condition. If he makes a waqf on his children and he has only one, or on his sons and he has only one son, half is for him and half for the poor. Thus al-Khaniyyah made equality between children and sons. Fath al-Qadir differentiated between them, saying: In children, the single one takes all; in sons, the single one does not take all. He said: It seems to be based on custom, and you know that the transmitted view is otherwise. If he makes a waqf on his sons, daughters do not deserve, and vice versa. The remaining branches related to waqf on children and relatives are known in al-Khassaf and others.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage provides a series of rulings on waqf made on children (awlad) and their offspring. It begins with a general principle: only the spoken words of the waqif matter, not the written document. Then it details who qualifies as 'walad' (child): it includes both males and females unless specified otherwise. Grandchildren (walad al-walad) do not inherit if there is a direct child. Waqf on 'awladi' (my children) excludes grandchildren in the apparent narration, but Qadikhan includes daughters' children in some contexts. The rules for multiple generations are given: if one child dies, his share goes to the poor unless three generations are named. There is a difference between waqf on 'awlad' (children) and 'banin' (sons): in al-Khaniyyah they are treated equally, but Fath al-Qadir differentiates based on custom. This passage is essentially a collection of memorization anchors for the student of fiqh. Note that these rulings are from the Hanafi school and are mufta bihi unless otherwise noted. The key distinction is between 'walad' (which can include females) and 'ibn' (which is specifically male).

Key Terms
الولد (al-walad): Child, including both males and females, but when qualified by 'ibn' it is male only.
ولد الولد (walad al-walad): Grandchild, who does not inherit from waqf in the presence of a direct child.
البطون (al-butun): Generations (literally bellies); referring to the layers of descendants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf is made on 'walad' (child) and the waqif has a son and a daughter, who receives the benefit?
A) Only the son
B) Both son and daughter
C) Only the daughter
D) The son and any grandson

Key Takeaway
For a Hanafi waqf on children, 'walad' includes both sexes, grandchildren are excluded unless direct children are absent, and generational distribution depends on the number of named generations.

Condition of Istibdal for the Waqif: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif's condition of replacement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on stipulating istibdal in a waqf, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The condition of istibdal for the waqif is disputed: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad voids the condition, but both agree the waqf stands.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute over a waqif's condition to replace the waqf property. While the mufta bihi follows Abu Yusuf's permission, understanding the disagreement sharpens your grasp of waqf perpetuity and the role of condition. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the claim of consensus on this issue is incorrect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
What exactly is the waqif stipulating? The source discusses the condition of istibdal (replacement) that the waqif includes for himself.
2
State the two main positions
Abu Yusuf permits the condition (the waqf and condition are both valid). Muhammad al-Shaybani invalidates the condition but upholds the waqf as valid.
3
Note the third position
Some scholars (transmitted by Qadikhan) hold that both the waqf and the condition are void if istibdal is stipulated.
4
Determine the dalil for each
Abu Yusuf relies on istihsan (juristic preference) and analogy to stipulating produce for oneself. Muhammad argues that the condition defeats the perpetuity (ta'bid) of waqf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its authority
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the permissibility of istibdal (Abu Yusuf's view), as preferred by later Hanafi authorities like Qutlizadah and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرع في الهداية على الاختلاف بين الشيخين شرط الاستبدال لنفسه فجوزه أبو يوسف وأبطل محمد الشرط وصحح التصحيح المنقول في اشتراط الغلة لنفسه تصحيحاً لهذا تأمل. قوله : (وأجمعوا أنه إذا شرط الاستبدال لنفسه الخ) مخالف لما . مر عن الهداية من تفريع المسألة على الاختلاف بين الشيخين، ثم رأيت في رسالة العلامة قتلي زاده في الاستبدال ما نصه وأما قولنا على الصحيح من المذهب فلان فيه خلاف أبي يوسف بن خالد السمني حيث ذهب إلى أن هذا الشرط باطل وإن كان الوقف بهذا الوجه صحيحاً. وذهب بعضهم إلى أن الوقف والشرط كلاهما باطلان كما نقله قاضيخان. وبهذا ظهر أن دعواه الإجماع في المسألة غير صحيحة وأن المسألة فيها خلاف لكن الصحيح رواية ودراية جواز الاستبدال اهـ. ورأيت في رسالة تحرير المقال في مسألة الاستبدال للشيخ المؤلف، ذكر أن بينهما مخالفة ظاهراً ثم قال : إلا أنه أي قاضيخان صور المسألة المختلف فيها بما إذا قال أرضي هذه صدقة
And in al-Hidayah, he branched on the difference between the two shaykhs [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] the condition of replacement for himself: Abu Yusuf permitted it, and Muhammad invalidated the condition, and corrected the transmitted correction in stipulating the produce for himself as a correction for this. Ponder. His statement: (And they unanimously agreed that if he stipulates replacement for himself...) contradicts what has passed in al-Hidayah of branching the issue on the difference between the two shaykhs. Then I saw in the treatise of 'Allamah Qutlizadah on replacement the following: As for our saying 'on the correct of the madhhab,' because there is a difference from Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samani who held that this condition is void although the waqf in this manner is valid. And some held that both the waqf and the condition are void, as transmitted by Qadikhan. By this it becomes clear that his claim of consensus on the issue is incorrect, and that the issue has difference, but the correct in transmission and knowledge is the permissibility of replacement. End. And I saw in the treatise Tahrir al-Maqal on the issue of replacement by the author shaykh, he mentioned that between them there is apparent disagreement, then said: 'Except that Qadikhan depicted the issue under dispute as when he says: "My land is sadaqah..." '
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of istibdal (replacement) of waqf property stipulated by the waqif for himself. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf permits it, while Muhammad al-Shaybani invalidates the condition but upholds the waqf. The author of al-Hidayah branches this on the earlier dispute about stipulating produce for oneself. The text then notes that a claim of consensus on this issue is incorrect; there is known disagreement from Abu Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samani and others. The correct view according to the author is permissibility of istibdal. Students should understand that istibdal is a complex issue; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is permissibility, but it is not universally accepted within the school. The authority weight: the dispute involves Sahibayn, so it is from the founding texts, but the later preference is for Abu Yusuf's facilitation.

Key Terms
الاستبدال (al-istibdal): The act of replacing waqf property with other property, often to avoid deterioration or increase benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, if a waqif stipulates the condition of istibdal (replacement) for himself, what is the ruling?
A) The condition is void and the waqf is void.
B) The condition is void but the waqf is valid.
C) The condition is valid and the waqf is valid.
D) The waqf is valid only if the condition is approved by a judge.

Key Takeaway
The condition of istibdal for the waqif is a genuine intra-Hanafi dispute; the mufta bihi permits it, but one must be aware of the contrary views within the school.
